# Prettier Conformance

Prettier was tsv's initial guide, and the formatter still tracks it for the common case ‚Äî but tsv has its own identity and makes **intentional, cataloged choices** to diverge where they're more defensible. This document catalogs those divergences along with bugs that tsv does not replicate.

## Terminology

**Matched**: tsv produces identical output to Prettier ‚Äî the goal and the common case (measure current rates with `deno task corpus:compare:format --all --summary`).

**Unmatched**: tsv produces different output. The suffix `_prettier_divergence` marks these fixtures. This document explains WHY for each case.

## Reasons tsv Differs

Each divergence is tagged with one or more `‚óÜreason` tokens ‚Äî single greppable
units (search `‚óÜ` for every tag, `‚óÜprettier_bug` for one category):

- `‚óÜspec_violation` ‚Äî Prettier emits spec-violating CSS/HTML/JS. tsv follows the spec
- `‚óÜspec_precedence` ‚Äî Prettier's output is valid but tsv emits the spec's canonical serialized form
- `‚óÜstable_quirk` ‚Äî Prettier preserves multiple forms without normalizing. tsv normalizes consistently
- `‚óÜprettier_bug` ‚Äî Prettier is non-idempotent, emits invalid output, or changes meaning (e.g. strips required parens). tsv produces stable, valid, meaning-preserving output
- `‚óÜparser_compat` ‚Äî Prettier's output breaks Svelte's parser. tsv produces Svelte-compatible output
- `‚óÜprint_width` ‚Äî Prettier allows lines to exceed printWidth. tsv breaks to stay within the limit
- `‚óÜbom_stripping` ‚Äî Prettier preserves byte-order marks. tsv strips them
- `‚óÜcomment_preservation` ‚Äî Prettier moves comments to a different syntactic position. tsv preserves comment position
- `‚óÜcontent_preservation` ‚Äî Prettier silently drops user comments. tsv preserves all comments
- `‚óÜdesign_choice` ‚Äî Other deliberate behavior differences, with rationale in the fixture

> Most `‚óÜcomment_preservation` and `‚óÜcontent_preservation` divergences live in the prose-form [TypeScript: Comments](#typescript-comments) and [CSS: Comments](#css-comments) catalogs, not the tag-prefixed catalog lists ‚Äî they're the largest divergence category but don't reduce to a single bullet.

### Prettier bug index

Every `‚óÜprettier_bug` ‚Äî cases where Prettier produces output that is non-idempotent, fails to re-parse, throws, or changes meaning, and tsv refuses to replicate. Grep `‚óÜprettier_bug` for each in context.

**Cataloged** (pinned by a fixture oracle or marker):

- CSS empty value + `!important` ‚Äî never converges (oscillates every pass) ‚Äî [empty_value_important](../tests/fixtures/css/values/variables/empty_value_important_prettier_divergence/)
- CSS escaped whitespace in a value (`50px\ ;`) ‚Äî drops the escape's payload, stranding the `\` onto the `;` / `)` ‚Üí output fails to re-parse; also splits an ident on an escaped `,` / `+`, and wraps a long value *inside* an escape ‚Äî [escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/values/escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/), [escaped_whitespace_long](../tests/fixtures/css/values/escaped_whitespace_long_prettier_divergence/)
- CSS escaped whitespace ending an at-rule prelude (`@layer a\ ;`) ‚Äî same, stranded onto the `;` ‚Üí the at-rule never ends; alone the output fails to re-parse, in context two at-rules silently merge ‚Äî [layer_escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/layer_escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/)
- CSS escaped whitespace ending a `url()` (`url(x\ )`) ‚Äî same, stranded onto the url's closing paren ‚Üí the token never terminates and the output fails to re-parse ‚Äî [url_escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/url_escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/)
- `<svelte:element this={'x'}>` ‚Äî ignores `singleQuote` and skips escaping ‚Üí invalid output (`this={"a"b"}`) ‚Äî [svelte_element_this_string](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/svelte_element_this_string_prettier_divergence/)
- `<svelte:element class="a  b">` ‚Äî fails to collapse repeated whitespace ‚Äî [svelte_element_class_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/svelte_element_class_whitespace_prettier_divergence/)
- Space after block element ‚Äî strands a leading space, non-idempotent ‚Äî [space_after_block](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/space_after_block_prettier_divergence/)
- Constrained `infer ‚Ä¶ extends` operand parens ‚Äî strips required parens ‚Üí output fails to re-parse ‚Äî [constrained_extends_parens](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/infer/constrained_extends_parens_prettier_divergence/)
- TS instantiation parens (`(x ? y : z)<T>`) ‚Äî strips parens, semantic change ‚Äî [instantiation_parens](../tests/fixtures/typescript/typescript_specific/assertions/instantiation_parens_prettier_divergence/); the class-operand / `export default` case (`export default (class {}<T>)`) is worse still (strips ‚Üí a class _declaration_) ‚Äî [export_default_instantiation](../tests/fixtures/typescript/modules/exports/default_wrappable_leftmost_operators/instantiation_prettier_divergence/)
- Svelte destructuring rename-with-default key drop (`{ a: b = 1 }` ‚Üí `{ b = 1 }`) ‚Äî semantic change ‚Äî [each](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/each/destructure_rename_default_prettier_divergence/), [await](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/destructure_rename_default_prettier_divergence/)
- `x?.#a` (optional chain to private field) ‚Äî throws on valid input (pinned by `prettier_rejects.txt`) ‚Äî [private_fields_optional_chain](../tests/fixtures/typescript/declarations/class/private_fields_optional_chain_prettier_divergence/)
- JSDoc cast + an enclosing paren ‚Äî emits the paren *between* the comment and its `(`, so the cast re-binds to the wider expression; non-idempotent, and a **semantic** change (oxfmt and biome share the bug) ‚Äî [jsdoc_type_cast_enclosing_parens](../tests/fixtures/typescript/syntax/comments/jsdoc_type_cast_enclosing_parens_prettier_divergence/)
- Bundler annotation (`/* @__PURE__ */`) + an enclosing paren ‚Äî same relocation, so the annotation ends up leading a paren instead of the call it marks and the call is no longer treated as side-effect-free; a **semantic** change, and unlike the cast prettier is *idempotent* on its own output, so nothing reveals it ‚Äî [pure_annotation_enclosing_parens](../tests/fixtures/typescript/syntax/comments/pure_annotation_enclosing_parens_prettier_divergence/)

**Prose-only** (no `output_prettier.*` oracle ‚Äî Prettier drops or throws, so the bug can't be pinned as a fixture):

- `import defer * as ns from 'm'` ‚Äî silently deletes the `defer` phase (information loss) ‚Äî ¬ßImport-phase proposals
- `import source x from 'm'` ‚Äî Prettier's TS printer throws (`'=' expected`) ‚Äî ¬ßImport-phase proposals
- `{@const y = /** @type {T} */ (z)}` ‚Äî Prettier emits invalid `(z}` then throws on its own output ‚Äî ¬ßJSDoc / paren semantics

## Decision Framework

**When to match Prettier:**

- Cosmetic choices (spacing preferences, quote styles)
- Output that's valid and reasonable
- Unclear which approach is "better"

**When to differ:** any reason in [Reasons tsv Differs](#reasons-tsv-differs) above. The two cross-cutting principles ‚Äî comment position and print width ‚Äî are detailed below.

### Comment Position Philosophy

**A formatter should not move a comment to a different syntactic position ‚Äî unless
the move is lossless and the position carries no authorship signal.** Comment
placement is usually a deliberate authoring choice ‚Äî it communicates what the comment
refers to ‚Äî so preserving it is tsv's default and its single largest category of
divergence from Prettier (see [TypeScript: Comments](#typescript-comments)).

Prettier's comment handling is its weakest area. It routinely moves comments from
between syntactic boundaries into adjacent blocks, parens, or other positions, changing
the apparent association ‚Äî and frequently **losing information** (two comments merging
onto one end-of-line, the second `//` becoming text; or reordering them). tsv treats
comment position as semantic and preserves it wherever that distinction is real.

**Principles:**

1. **Comments between an operator and its operand stay there.** If the user wrote
   `? foo : // about bar`, the comment stays after `:`. Prettier moves it to trailing
   on `foo`, changing its association from the false branch to the true branch.
2. **Trailing comments stay trailing.** `foo // comment` keeps the comment on `foo`.
3. **Same-line block comments stay same-line.** `extends T /* c */ ?` keeps the
   comment after `T`, not moved after `?`.
4. **Both positions are valid when dual-stable.** When the user's chosen position is
   idempotent, preserve it. Don't collapse to one canonical form ‚Äî that destroys the
   distinction between "comment about X" and "comment about Y".
5. **The deciding test is information loss, not position purity.** Preserve a comment's
   position when relocating it would lose information ‚Äî the canonical case is Prettier's
   end-of-line relocation *merging* two comments onto one line (the second `//` becomes
   text) or reordering them; tsv keeps them distinct (the name‚Üí`=`/`:`/`?` binding
   divergences). But where relocating is **lossless** *and* the position carries no
   signal ‚Äî a same-line line comment past a *pure separator*, e.g. a list element's
   comma (`A // c‚èé, B` ‚Üí `A, // c`; the comma is structure and the comment trails the
   element either way) ‚Äî tsv trails like Prettier rather than manufacturing a divergence
   for a meaningless distinction.

**When reviewing comment-related fixes:** Default to preserving position. Match
Prettier's repositioning only when the move is lossless *and* the position carries no
authorship signal (a pure-separator trail), or when the original position is clearly
wrong (e.g., comment inside a token boundary). Otherwise ‚Äî and whenever relocating
would merge, reorder, or drop a comment ‚Äî preserve and create a `_prettier_divergence`
fixture.

### Uniform Forced-Continuation Indent

A direct corollary of comment-position preservation, and tsv's most cross-cutting
comment-layout rule. When a **line** comment forces part of a construct onto a new
line ‚Äî a `//` runs to end-of-line, so whatever the author wrote after it cannot stay
on that line ‚Äî tsv keeps the comment where it was written and drops the following
token to a continuation line **indented one level**. The continuation then reads as
part of its construct, not as a sibling statement or member.

One rule, applied at every site where a line comment splits a construct's head from
its tail:

- **Declaration and module headers** ‚Äî keyword‚Üíname, keyword‚Üí`{`, binding‚Üí`from`,
  `*`‚Üí`as`, and every other header gap (`import // c‚èé{ a } from 'm'`,
  `export // c‚èéconst x = 1`). See [Declaration- and module-header line-comment
  continuation indent](#comment-relocation).
- **Prefix type operators** ‚Äî the `keyof`/`typeof` operand hang
  (`type A = keyof // c‚èé\t\tB`), shared via `append_keyword_value_line_comments` with
  type-parameter constraint/default values and class-property initializers. See
  [Prefix type-operator operand hang](#comment-relocation).
- **`: Type` annotations** ‚Äî the colon‚Üítype continuation (`prop: // c‚èé\tType`), via
  the shared `build_type_annotation_doc`, **uniformly for union, intersection, and
  simple types** and in **every** context: property signatures
  ([annotation_simple](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/comments/annotation_simple_prettier_divergence/)),
  variable declarations, class properties, function parameters/return types, and
  intersection types
  ([annotation_continuation_indent](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/comments/annotation_continuation_indent_prettier_divergence/)),
  plus an index signature's key-type
  ([index_signature_key_type_line_comments](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/type_members/index_signature_key_type_line_comments_prettier_divergence/))
  and value-type
  ([index_signature_value_line_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/type_members/index_signature_value_line_comment_prettier_divergence/)).
- **Before-`:` key/binding gap** ‚Äî the complement of the colon‚Üítype case: a line
  comment between a key/binding name (or its `?`/`!` marker) and the `:`
  (`prop // c‚èé\t\t: T`) keeps the comment after the marker and indents the whole
  `: type` continuation one level, via the shared `build_marker_colon_line_continuation`.
  Uniform across index signatures
  ([index_signature_key_colon_line_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/type_members/index_signature_key_colon_line_comment_prettier_divergence/)),
  property signatures and class properties ‚Äî key‚Üí`:`
  ([key_colon_line_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/syntax/comments/key_colon_line_comment_prettier_divergence/))
  and `?`‚Üí`:`
  ([optional_marker_line_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/syntax/comments/optional_marker_line_comment_prettier_divergence/)),
  variable bindings
  ([binding_key_colon_line_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/declarations/variable/binding_key_colon_line_comment_prettier_divergence/)),
  and function parameters
  ([param_key_colon_line_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/declarations/function/param_key_colon_line_comment_prettier_divergence/)).
  Prettier keeps the continuation flush ‚Äî and for property signatures / class
  properties relocates the comment to end-of-line.
- **Index-signature bracket gaps** ‚Äî the `]`‚Üívalue-`:` continuation
  (`[k: T] // c‚èé\t: V`). See [Index signature `]`‚Üívalue-`:`](#comment-relocation).

The indent is tsv's own layout choice; prettier handles each site differently ‚Äî it
relocates the comment (into braces/parens, after `from`/`as`/`;`), floats it past
`;`, keeps the continuation **flush**, or drops the comment onto its own line. So
this rule is a deliberate `_prettier_divergence` everywhere it bites: where prettier
**indents** the declarator (`const`/`let`/`var` keyword‚Üídeclarator) it agrees, a
regular fixture; the multi-member union after `:` is a divergence (prettier drops the comment
onto its own line). The payoff is
internal consistency: every forced continuation reads the same regardless of which
construct the comment split.

### Authored breaks in value position

The complement of [¬ßUniform Forced-Continuation Indent](#uniform-forced-continuation-indent),
and the rule that decides when that one applies at all. A **line** comment *forces* a
break ‚Äî `//` runs to end-of-line, so the tail cannot stay on the line, and the only
question left is how far to indent it. A **block** comment forces nothing: `x = /* c */ y`
is legal on one line, so a break after `/* c */` is the author's, not the comment's.

**tsv reflows an unforced break in value position.** A line break between a value gap's
head and its value carries no meaning tsv preserves ‚Äî it is ordinary layout, and the TS
printer decides layout by width. This holds uniformly across every value position:
`const`/`let`/`export const` `=`, `type =`, `export =`, `export default`, assignment
expressions, class-property initializers, object-literal values, parameter defaults,
arrow bodies, `:` annotations, return types, `satisfies`, and `as`.

Prettier preserves the break at some of these sites and reflows it at others, so this is a
deliberate divergence wherever prettier happens to preserve. The payoff is the same as the
forced-continuation rule's: one answer regardless of which construct the comment sits in.

Two comment shapes are **outside** this rule, because their break is not unforced layout ‚Äî
they hang the value, and the gate is the shared `comment_hangs_next`:

- A **line** comment forces the break (`//` runs to end-of-line), so the value drops to a
  continuation indented one level ‚Äî [¬ßUniform Forced-Continuation
  Indent](#uniform-forced-continuation-indent).
- A **multiline** block the author broke after (`kw /* ‚Ä¶‚èé‚Ä¶ */‚èév`) hangs the value; one whose
  value shares its closing line (`kw /* ‚Ä¶‚èé‚Ä¶ */ v`) stays inline, the way prettier keeps it.

A **blank line** inside the gap **yields with the break**. `A = /* c */‚èé‚èé1` formats to
`A = /* c */ 1`, the same fixed point as the single-newline authoring. This is not a second
rule but a consequence of the first: a blank line is a property of a line break, so once the
break is judged unforced and reflowed there are no longer two lines for the blank to
separate. Elsewhere tsv treats a blank line as Tier-1 authoring intent and preserves it ‚Äî
that still holds, and it is what decides this case rather than contradicting it. The blank
survives exactly where the break survives, which is the **own-line** authoring
(`= ‚èé/* c */‚èé‚èév`): there the comment does occupy its own line, the break is forced, and both
the break and the blank are kept. An author who wants the blank writes that form.

The rule holds at every value gap whose own-line authoring **hangs** the comment (the
initializer family: declarator, class property, object value, enum member, and the `=`/`:`
gaps that share their emitters).

**Known residual.** Two gaps still keep the blank: `await`‚Üíoperand and `new`‚Üícallee (inside a
declarator; a bare expression statement has no group to collapse into, so it holds the break
regardless of width). Those emitters **relocate** an own-line comment up onto the head line
while the leading run picks its separator from the comment's *authored* position, so the two
disagree: pass 1 relocates and keeps the break, pass 2 sees a now-glued comment and collapses
it. That is not a stable resting place ‚Äî it is a **non-idempotent format**, and the blank is
incidental to it.

The import/export header family had the same defect and is now fixed. The diagnosis there was
**not** a comment-position question: `gap_comment_continuation_tail` simply never consulted its
gate, keying the choice on line-vs-block alone while `comment_hangs_next` ‚Äî the shared
keyword‚Üívalue rule its `export default` / `export =` siblings already use ‚Äî says a single-line
block collapses from *any* authored position. Routing the emitter through that gate made all 19
header gaps idempotent and is what `export * from` needed too (it had been the lone header gap
preserving the break, for want of the same collapse). The same shape is the likely fix for the
two remaining gaps: ask the gate, don't re-derive the answer at the call site.

Prettier is split here and not along tsv's line: it preserves the blank for a declarator and
an object value while collapsing it (with a relocation) for a class property, a parameter
default, and an enum member. Neither tool follows the other, so prettier is not the tiebreak;
the rule above is tsv's own, and it is a deliberate divergence wherever prettier preserves.

One site deliberately keeps a blank the rule would drop: a **conditional branch** ‚Äî the
expression ternary's (`a ? /* c */‚èé‚èéb`, via `comment_followed_by_blank`) and the
conditional type's (`T extends U ? X : /* c */‚èé‚èéY`, via the branch-gap run's blank arm)
alike ‚Äî where the blank is itself a break trigger because prettier breaks on it too. There
the break survives, so the blank does ‚Äî consistent with the rule, by a gate that forces
the break rather than an exception to it.

The rule is scoped to **value gaps** (head‚Üívalue: `=`, `:`, `as`, a keyword). A **list** gap
is governed by ordinary blank-line preservation instead ‚Äî a blank between two list items is
authoring tsv keeps, so an array element's leading comment preserves it
([arrays/end_of_line_block_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/arrays/end_of_line_block_comment_prettier_divergence/)).
The printer names the split as the two leading-run modes `AdjacentValueGap` and `Adjacent`.

Distinct from all of the above: a comment prettier **relocates** across the gap (`enum`
`A = /* c */‚èé1` ‚Üí `A /* c */ = 1`; binary `b + /* c */‚èéc` ‚Üí `b /* c */ + c`) is a
comment-*position* divergence, governed by [¬ßComment Position
Philosophy](#comment-position-philosophy), not by this rule.

### Print Width Philosophy

**Prettier treats `printWidth` as a soft target.** Lines may exceed it in various edge cases (fill algorithm boundaries, block expressions, template literals, certain constructs that "don't look good" when wrapped).

**tsv treats `printWidth` as a hard limit.** If content exceeds 100 characters, tsv breaks it when possible. This is a deliberate design choice affecting many divergences in this document:

- Block expression conditions (`{#if}`, `{#each}`, etc.) with logical operators
- Template literal interpolations
- Fill algorithm edge cases (101-char boundaries)
- Single-specifier imports
- Various "short expression" tolerances

The benefit: predictable output that respects the configured line length. The tradeoff: some constructs may break where Prettier would keep them inline.

**"When possible" has two systematic exceptions.**

*Whitespace-sensitive content.* Inside `<pre>` / `<textarea>` a line break *is* content, so print width yields to render semantics and an over-width line stands ‚Äî those elements never reach the shared layout analysis (see [¬ßSvelte: Inline content block-style](#svelte-inline-content-block-style)). Both formatters agree there, so it is not a divergence; it is pinned by [fill_tail_after_expr_pre](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_tail_after_expr_pre_long/), whose two cases are the same overflowing fill in a `<pre>` and a `<textarea>`.

*A `{tag}` welded to a preceding word.* When a `{expr}` / `{@html}` / `{@render}` tag is glued to the end of a text word with no whitespace (`‚Ä¶ tsv is ~{ratio}`), tsv keeps it on that word's line and lets it overflow rather than breaking *before* the word to hold ‚â§ 100 ‚Äî prettier keeps the tag *outside* the text fill, so the fill never sees its width and never breaks before the word it is welded to, and tsv matches. Both formatters agree, so it is not a divergence; it is pinned by [fill_leading_line](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_leading_line/). A tag *separated* from the preceding word by whitespace still breaks before the tag to hold ‚â§ 100 ([fill_break_before_expr_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_break_before_expr_long_prettier_divergence/)): there the whitespace boundary sits *directly before the tag*, and tsv breaks it (its hard limit outranks prettier, which overflows to 101). The welded case has no boundary before the tag ‚Äî it abuts the word with no space ‚Äî so the nearest break falls *before the welded word* (`~`), which would carry that word onto the next line with the tag rather than isolate it; tsv declines that break and keeps the word in place, matching prettier's tag-outside-the-fill layout.

Everywhere else, a line tsv *can* break is a line tsv *does* break.

---

## Catalog

### CSS: At-Rules

- Escaped whitespace ending a prelude ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [layer_escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/layer_escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/)
- Escaped control char in an at-rule name ‚Äî ‚óÜparser_compat ‚Äî [name_escaped_control_char](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/name_escaped_control_char_prettier_divergence/)
- @container spacing ‚Äî ‚óÜspec_violation ‚Äî [container_spacing](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/container_spacing_prettier_divergence/)
- @container empty feature value ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [container_empty_feature_value](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/container_empty_feature_value_prettier_divergence/)
- @container line wrap ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [container_long](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/container_long_prettier_divergence/)
- @import line wrap ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [import_media_query_long](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/import_media_query_long_prettier_divergence/)
- @media boolean spacing ‚Äî ‚óÜspec_violation ‚Äî [media_boolean_spacing](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/media_boolean_spacing_prettier_divergence/)
- @media line wrap ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [media_long](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/media_long_prettier_divergence/)
- @scope whitespace ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [scope_complex](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scope_complex_prettier_divergence/)
- @scope newlines ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [scope_selector](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scope_selector_prettier_divergence/)
- @supports line wrap ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [supports_long](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/supports_long_prettier_divergence/)
- @scope `to` keyword case ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [scope_to_case](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scope_to_case_prettier_divergence/)
- @scope empty-root spacing ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî tsv keeps a consistent space before the clause paren (`@scope ()`), where prettier collapses it (`@scope()`) only for the empty-root-only prelude (the forgiving-list acceptance otherwise matches prettier ‚Äî see [scope_forgiving_selector_list](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scope_forgiving_selector_list/)) ‚Äî [scope_empty_root](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scope_empty_root_prettier_divergence/)
- Media grouped feature case ‚Äî ‚óÜparser_compat ‚Äî [media_grouped_feature_case](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/media_grouped_feature_case_prettier_divergence/)
- SCSS directive numbers ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [scss_directive_number_preserved](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scss_directive_number_preserved_prettier_divergence/)

**Escaped whitespace ending a prelude**: an at-rule prelude can end in an escaped whitespace (`@layer a\ ;` ‚Äî the layer is named `a `, since `\ ` is a valid escape whose escaped code point IS that space, css-syntax-3 ¬ß4.3.4/¬ß4.3.7). tsv preserves it. Prettier trims it as padding, stranding the backslash onto the `;`, which it then escapes: alone, prettier's output no longer parses (tsv rejects `@layer a\;` with `Expected '{' or ';' after 'at-rule prelude'`); in context it parses but the prelude swallows everything up to the next `{`, silently **merging two at-rules into one**. Prettier gets the block form right (`@layer b\ {`), where the payload space already separates the prelude from the brace ‚Äî and tsv likewise adds no second separator there. Same rule, same reason as [CSS: Values ¬ßEscaped whitespace in a value](#css-values). See [layer_escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/layer_escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/).

**Escaped control char in an at-rule name**: an escape *inside the at-rule name token* (`@m\A x`) is part of the name ‚Äî Svelte's `parseCss` (and tsv, matching it) decode the whole run to the name (`"m\nx"`, a control char mid-name), with an empty prelude. Postcss/prettier instead **split** the name at the escape into a name plus a prelude (`@m \A x {`), and reject outright when the name *starts* with an escape (`@\6D edia` ‚Üí "At-rule without name"). tsv can't adopt prettier's split without contradicting its own parse, so it emits the name from **source**, preserving the escape verbatim (`@m\A x {`) ‚Äî the decoded control char never lands raw in the output. Emitting the *decoded* form (the prior bug) injected a raw newline, corrupting the file, and dropped the escape on reparse (name `m\nx` ‚Üí `m`) ‚Äî content loss and a broken fixed point. Same escape-preservation rule as escaped property names, which both formatters keep verbatim (`escaped_property_name`, no divergence). The end-of-name subcase (`@n\A {`, the escape needs a terminator space) adds no second separator before `{`, the same absorption as [Escaped whitespace ending a prelude](#css-at-rules) above. See [name_escaped_control_char](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/name_escaped_control_char_prettier_divergence/).

**Spec violations**: CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß4.3.4 specifies that an identifier immediately followed by `(` tokenizes as a `<function-token>`, not as an `<ident-token>` plus `(`. Media Queries 4 ¬ß3 explicitly notes: "Whitespace is required between a 'not', 'and', or 'or' keyword and the following '(' character, because without it that would instead parse as a `<function-token>`." Container Queries (CSS Conditional 5) use the same grammar pattern. Prettier normalizes this for `@supports` but not `@media` or `@container`.

**SCSS directive numbers**: SCSS/Sass directives (`@include`, `@mixin`, `@if`, `@for`, `@each`, `@while`, `@function`, `@return`, `@debug`) are not standard CSS. Per CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß5.4.2 an unknown at-rule's prelude is consumed as an opaque list of component values with no defined grammar, so tsv preserves it verbatim (e.g. `@include foo(.5s)` stays `.5s`, `@include baz(1.50)` stays `1.50`). Prettier keeps a hardcoded SCSS-directive list whose params it re-parses as a value AST and number-normalizes (`.5s`‚Üí`0.5s`, `1.50`‚Üí`1.5`). tsv applies number normalization only to contexts whose grammar it parses ‚Äî declaration values and `@media`/`@supports` preludes (see [CSS: Values](#css-values) "Number dot-ident"); unrecognized directive preludes stay raw. Both outputs are valid CSS (`.5` and `0.5` are the same `<number>` token); the divergence is one of scope, not correctness.

**Media comma-list wrapping (not a divergence)**: a comma-separated `@media` query list (Media Queries 4 ¬ß"media query list") that exceeds print width is broken at every top-level comma ‚Äî one query per line, one indent level ‚Äî matching Prettier exactly. The `@media line wrap` divergence below applies only to a _single_ `and`-joined query (no comma), which Prettier never wraps but tsv does.

**CSS keyword case ‚Äî the canonicalize/preserve line.** CSS keywords are ASCII case-insensitive (CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß"tokenizing"). tsv adopts prettier's canonicalization set wholesale ‚Äî it **lowercases** property names, at-rule names, units, pseudo-class/element names, media-feature names, keyframe `from`/`to`, hex, and `!important`, and **preserves** values (`color: RED`), custom properties (`--MyVar`), type/element selectors (`DIV`, SVG `linearGradient`), function names (`URL(`/`RGB(`), media types (`SCREEN`), and the `not`/`only` media qualifiers ‚Äî matching prettier on both sides. tsv parses every case-insensitive keyword (so `@supports (a: b) AND (c: d)`, `@media screen AND (‚Ä¶)`, `:NTH-CHILD(2n+1)` all parse ‚Äî Class-1 correctness) but only rewrites the spelling where prettier does. The lone exception is unit case: tsv lowercases **all** units to their spec-canonical serialized form, including `Hz`/`kHz`/`Q`, where prettier upcases instead ‚Äî see "Unit serialization case" under [CSS: Values](#css-values).

The boolean **connectors** `and`/`or`/`not` are **preserved** (`@supports (a: b) AND (c: d)` keeps `AND`), matching prettier: uppercase boolean operators are a recognized "logical-skeleton" readability signal (the SQL convention), so their case carries authorial intent ‚Äî the same principle that keeps comment position. This is verified by the regular [supports_connector_case](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/supports_connector_case/), [container_connector_case](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/container_connector_case/), and [media_connector_case](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/media_connector_case/) fixtures (no `_prettier_divergence` suffix ‚Äî tsv matches prettier).

**@scope `to` keyword case** is the lone deliberate keyword-case *canonicalization* divergence (the `Media grouped feature case` below also differs on a feature name's case, but that's a parser-compat consequence of leaving grouped conditions opaque, not a canonicalization choice). `to` is a **delimiter** keyword (it marks the scope limit ‚Äî a position marker, not a boolean operator, like keyframe `from`/`to`), so tsv canonicalizes it to lowercase for consistency with how it lowercases keyframe `from`/`to`. Prettier inconsistently lowercases keyframe `from`/`to` but **preserves** `@scope`'s `TO`; tsv lowercases both delimiter keywords uniformly. So `@scope (.card) TO (.footer)` ‚Üí tsv `to`, prettier `TO`. See [scope_to_case](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scope_to_case_prettier_divergence/).

**Media feature-name case**: a media-feature *name* is ASCII case-insensitive (Media Queries 4 ¬ß"Syntax"), and prettier lowercases it (`@media (MIN-WIDTH: 100px)` ‚Üí `(min-width: 100px)`, including the range/boolean forms `(WIDTH >= 600px)` and `(HOVER)`) while preserving media types (`SCREEN`), the `and`/`or`/`not`/`only` keywords, and feature *values* (`(orientation: LANDSCAPE)` keeps `LANDSCAPE`). tsv **matches** prettier here for **simple** feature expressions ‚Äî covered by the regular [media_feature_case](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/media_feature_case/) (no `_prettier_divergence` suffix). A feature whose *value* is a function (`(min-width: calc(‚Ä¶))`, `(width: min(‚Ä¶))`) is still simple: the function's parentheses don't make the feature opaque, so its name lowercases like any other ‚Äî covered by [media_feature_function_value](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/media_feature_function_value/). Custom media names (`--*`) are case-sensitive (CSS Variables 1) and preserved. The one divergence is **grouped** conditions (`((a) and (b))`, `(not (x))`): prettier's media-query parser only partially descends ‚Äî lowercasing the first nested feature and leaving the rest ‚Äî whereas tsv treats the whole grouped condition as opaque and leaves it verbatim, so its nested features are handled consistently. See [media_grouped_feature_case](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/media_grouped_feature_case_prettier_divergence/). Note `@import`'s media-query feature names are preserved by both formatters (prettier doesn't run them through media-feature parsing), so tsv leaves them too.

### CSS: Selectors

- Column combinator `||` ‚Äî ‚óÜparser_compat ‚Äî [column](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/combinators/column_prettier_divergence/)
- Consecutive combinators (`> > .a`, `+ ~ .d`, glued `>>.a`) ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [consecutive_combinator](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/consecutive_combinator_svelte_prettier_divergence/): a run of combinators with no compound between them. tsv **preserves** every authored combinator (normalizing only the whitespace to single spaces, so glued `>>.a` ‚Üí `> > .a`); prettier **collapses** a whitespace-separated run to its last (`> > .a` ‚Üí `> .a`, in `output_prettier`) and *freezes* a glued run verbatim (`>>.a`, pinned by `prettier_variant_glued`). tsv declines the collapse because it is lossy ‚Äî the dropped combinator is authorship the diagnostics layer needs (parseCss collapses too, an AST divergence ‚Äî see [conformance_svelte.md ¬ßCSS Corrections](./conformance_svelte.md#css-corrections)). A *trailing* combinator (`.a > > {}`) rejects in both
- :nth-child() An+B ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [nth_child](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_class/nth_child_prettier_divergence/)
- An+B leading `+` in pseudo-args ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [nth_leading_plus](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_class/nth_leading_plus_prettier_divergence/): a bare An+B term inside functional pseudo-class args (`:foo(+2n + 1)`, `:is(+3)`, `:not(+n)`) is a single `Nth` (Svelte's `parseCss`, which tsv matches), so tsv keeps the leading `+` glued to its coefficient; prettier reads the leading `+` as a combinator and spaces it (`:foo(+ 2n + 1)`). A leading `-` doesn't diverge (both keep `-n + 3` glued)
- :nth-child(‚Ä¶ of S) `of` spacing ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [nth_child_of](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_class/nth_child_of_svelte_prettier_divergence/): tsv always emits single spaces around `of`; prettier collapses whitespace runs there but never inserts an absent space, so a glued `of.class` stays glued
- Pseudo-args indent (single compound) ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [compound_args_indent](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_class/compound_args_indent_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Nested pseudo-args indent ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [nested_where_is](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_class/nested_where_is_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Control-char combinator whitespace (VT `U+000B` / FF `U+000C`) ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [combinator_control_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/combinator_control_whitespace_prettier_divergence/): a descendant combinator authored with VT or FF ‚Äî both in JS `\s`, so Svelte's `parseCss` (and tsv, matching it) tokenize them as the descendant combinator ‚Äî normalizes to a single space, uniform with tab/newline gaps; prettier freezes the raw byte. FF is spec-whitespace via input preprocessing (‚ÜíLF); VT is a non-printable the spec excludes, where tsv follows Svelte over css-syntax. NBSP and other Unicode spaces are preserved by both, so only the ASCII C0 pair diverges.

**Pseudo-args indent**: When a pseudo-class/element's argument list breaks, prettier indents it an extra level if the enclosing compound's flat `selector-selector` node count exceeds 2 (`shouldIndent = node.nodes.length > 2` in `printer-postcss.js`). That extra `indent` exists to align the continuation lines of a complex selector broken at its combinators; for a *single* compound (no combinator) there is no continuation to align, so it only nests the pseudo args one level deeper than the rule body. tsv keys the indent on combinator presence instead ‚Äî a complex selector that spans more than one compound indents its continuation (matching prettier), and a pseudo's broken args always indent exactly one level relative to their pseudo. So a combinator-bearing selector matches prettier, while a single compound's pseudo args sit one level in with the `)` aligned to the selector it closes. Uniform, and no node counting. Combinator-bearing case (which matches prettier): [combinators/pseudo_args_long](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/combinators/pseudo_args_long/).

### CSS: Values

- Ratio in media queries ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [ratio](../tests/fixtures/css/values/ratio/ratio_prettier_divergence/)
- Transform list wrap ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [transform_long](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/transform_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Space-separated value wrap ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [space_separated_long_wrap](../tests/fixtures/css/values/lists/space_separated_long_wrap_prettier_divergence/)
- Comma+space value boundary ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [comma_space_separated_long](../tests/fixtures/css/values/lists/comma_space_separated_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Number dot-ident ‚Äî ‚óÜspec_violation ‚Äî [number_dot_ident](../tests/fixtures/css/values/numbers/number_dot_ident_prettier_divergence/)
- Trailing double-dot ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [trailing_double_dot](../tests/fixtures/css/values/numbers/trailing_double_dot_prettier_divergence/)
- Block-valued custom prop ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [block_value](../tests/fixtures/css/values/variables/block_value_svelte_prettier_divergence/)
- Empty custom-prop value ‚Äî ‚óÜstable_quirk ‚Äî [empty_value](../tests/fixtures/css/values/variables/empty_value_prettier_divergence/)
- Empty value + `!important` ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [empty_value_important](../tests/fixtures/css/values/variables/empty_value_important_prettier_divergence/)
- var() value-less fallback ‚Äî ‚óÜspec_precedence ‚Äî [var_empty_fallback_degenerate](../tests/fixtures/css/values/variables/var_empty_fallback_degenerate_prettier_divergence/)
- Unit serialization case ‚Äî ‚óÜspec_precedence ‚Äî [units_serialize_case](../tests/fixtures/css/values/units_serialize_case_prettier_divergence/)
- Unquoted url() content opaque ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [url_nested_reformat](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/url_nested_reformat_prettier_divergence/)
- Escaped-paren url() whitespace ‚Äî ‚óÜspec_precedence ‚Äî [url_escaped_paren_ws](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/url_escaped_paren_ws_prettier_divergence/)
- Escaped whitespace in a value ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/values/escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/)
- Escaped whitespace in a long value ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [escaped_whitespace_long](../tests/fixtures/css/values/escaped_whitespace_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Escaped whitespace at the end of a url() ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [url_escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/url_escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/)
- String glued to a non-ASCII space ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [comma_string_nonascii_space](../tests/fixtures/css/values/lists/comma_string_nonascii_space_prettier_divergence/)
- Single value glued to a non-ASCII space ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [boundary_nonascii_space](../tests/fixtures/css/values/boundary_nonascii_space_prettier_divergence/)
- Glued run of quoted strings ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [glued_string_run](../tests/fixtures/css/values/glued_string_run_prettier_divergence/)

**Space-separated value wrap**: Prettier doesn't wrap CSS space-separated values (e.g., `box-shadow`) when they exceed print width. A 101-char `box-shadow: var(--a) color-mix(...)` stays on one line. tsv wraps at the print width boundary, breaking between space-separated values. This respects the configured print width rather than allowing arbitrary overflows.

**Comma+space value boundary**: When comma-separated values contain space-separated parts (like multiple `box-shadow` values), Prettier tolerates lines exceeding printWidth. tsv breaks to stay within 100 chars. See `comma_space_separated_long/` for the matching behavior at 100 and 102 chars.

**Number dot-ident**: tsv matches Prettier's number normalization for all valid CSS ‚Äî scientific-notation exponents (`1E+2`‚Üí`1e2`, `5e0`‚Üí`5`), trailing/leading zeros (`1.50`‚Üí`1.5`, `.5`‚Üí`0.5`), and a trailing dot before a terminator (`1.`‚Üí`1`, `1.e1`‚Üí`1e1`). This applies to declaration values and to `@media`/`@supports` preludes; `@container` preludes are left raw, matching Prettier. The lone divergence is the _invalid_ sequence `<number>.<ident>` (e.g. `1.px`, `1.foo`): Prettier merges it into a dimension (`1px`), but per CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß4.3.3 that is three tokens (`<number>` `<delim .>` `<ident>`), not a dimension ‚Äî so tsv preserves the source verbatim. This only arises in invalid CSS; Prettier itself keeps `url(1.png)` unmerged.

**Trailing double-dot**: A malformed number with a *consecutive* double dot (`1..`, `1..e-10`, `1..5`) ‚Äî `parseCss` accepts it (stored raw). The number tokenizer strips a *single* trailing dot (`1.` ‚Üí `1`), but stripping one from `1..` and re-gluing the leftover onto the next token (`1..e-10` ‚Üí `1.e-10`) re-parses as a number and normalizes again on the next pass (an F1 non-idempotency). tsv therefore leaves the whole malformed run **verbatim** ‚Äî uniform with the other malformed-dot forms it already preserves (`..5`, `1.5.5`, `1.px`; see "Number dot-ident" above). Prettier normalizes it (`1..` ‚Üí `1`, `1..e-10` ‚Üí `1e-10`, some over two passes ‚Äî its own transient non-idempotency). Only arises on malformed input.

**Block-valued custom property**: A custom property whose entire value is a top-level `{...}` block is valid per CSS Variables Level 1 ¬ß2.1 (`<declaration-value>`, any token sequence with balanced brackets) and appears in Prettier's own corpus. Prettier formats the block contents on their own indented lines like a nested rule body (closing `}` on its own line, then `;`); tsv preserves the value as a single opaque single-line expression. Both forms are stable/idempotent under their respective formatters. (Svelte's CSS parser rejects this form outright with `css_expected_identifier`, so this is also a `_svelte_divergence` ‚Äî see [conformance_svelte.md](./conformance_svelte.md).)

**Empty custom-property value**: An empty custom-property value is valid ‚Äî `<declaration-value>?` is optional (CSS Variables 1 ¬ß"Custom Property Value Syntax"). CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß"Consume a declaration" trims leading **and** trailing whitespace from a declaration's value, so `--a:;`, `--a: ;`, and `--a:     ;` all parse to the same empty value; the spacing is not significant. Prettier preserves whatever spacing the source has (multiple stable forms ‚Äî `prettier_variant_compact`/`prettier_variant_spaces`); tsv normalizes to a single space (`--a: ;`), the form CSS Variables 1 ¬ß"Serializing Custom Properties" mandates ("an empty custom property ‚Ä¶ must serialize with a single space as its value"). Non-custom empty declarations (`color:;`) remain a parse error ‚Äî a value is required there. A variant ‚Äî an empty custom-property value carrying `!important` (`--a: !important;`) ‚Äî exposes a prettier **non-convergence** bug: prettier adds a space before `!important` on every pass (`--a:!important` ‚Üí `--a: !important` ‚Üí `--a:  !important` ‚Üí ‚Ä¶) and never reaches a fixed point, so it can't serve as a formatter oracle. tsv normalizes to the single-space form and is idempotent; guarded by [empty_value_important](../tests/fixtures/css/values/variables/empty_value_important_prettier_divergence/), whose `prettier_nonconvergent.txt` marker makes the validator live-verify the non-convergence (rule F5) instead of running the prettier-anchored rules.

**var() value-less fallback**: A `var()` whose fallback contains no real token ‚Äî only commas/whitespace (`var(--a,,)`) ‚Äî has a value-less fallback whose canonical form is `var(--a,)` (CSS Syntax 3 trims the fallback whitespace; a value-less `<declaration-value>?` is empty). tsv normalizes to that canonical form; prettier instead settles on the degenerate `var(--a, ,)` (preserving the extra comma, just normalizing spacing ‚Äî stable in one pass), pinned via the `prettier_variant_*` fixture. Pathological input (never in real CSS). The valid empty-fallback round-trip ‚Äî where tsv and prettier agree in one pass ‚Äî is the regular fixture [var_empty_fallback](../tests/fixtures/css/values/variables/var_empty_fallback/).

**Unit serialization case**: CSS dimension units are ASCII case-insensitive (CSS Syntax 3) and their canonical **serialized** form is lowercase ‚Äî including the frequency units `Hz`/`kHz` and the quarter-millimeter `Q`. CSS Values 4 ¬ß7.3 states "all `<frequency>` units are compatible, and `hz` is their canonical unit" and that "1Hz serializes as 1hz"; ¬ß6.2 likewise gives "1Q serializes as 1q". tsv canonicalizes **every** unit to this lowercase serialized form (`440Hz`‚Üí`440hz`, `1kHz`‚Üí`1khz`, `10Q`‚Üí`10q`), the same rule it applies to `PX`‚Üí`px`. Prettier instead **upcases** these three to their prose spelling (`Hz`/`kHz`/`Q`) while lowercasing all other units; tsv follows the spec's canonical form (spec precedence), so they stay lowercase. The all-agree units are the regular [units_case](../tests/fixtures/css/values/units_case/); the `Hz`/`kHz`/`Q` trio is the divergence, [units_serialize_case](../tests/fixtures/css/values/units_serialize_case_prettier_divergence/).

**Unquoted url() content opaque**: Per CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß4.3.6 an unquoted `url(...)` is consumed as one opaque `<url-token>` ‚Äî its content is *not* re-parsed as component values ‚Äî so tsv preserves it **verbatim** (`url(a(b,c))` and `url(a( b ))` each format to themselves). When the content contains a nested `(...)` group, prettier instead treats it as a value and reformats inside it: `url(a(b,c))` ‚Üí `url(a(b, c))` (a space is added after the comma) and `url(a( b ))` ‚Üí `url(a(b))` (the interior whitespace is dropped). tsv is the more defensible side ‚Äî reformatting inside an opaque token is a divergence, not a normalization ‚Äî and both formatters keep their own output idempotent. Only a nested `(...)` exposes it; flat url content has nothing to reformat, and a quoted `url("‚Ä¶")` is a string both leave alone. On Prettier's own corpus this surfaces in `tests/format/css/inline-url/inline_url.css` (`url(--var(foo-bar,#dadce0))` ‚Üí `url(--var(foo-bar, #dadce0))`) and `tests/format/css/loose/loose.css` (`url(var( x ))` ‚Üí `url(var(x))`). See [url_nested_reformat](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/url_nested_reformat_prettier_divergence/).

**Escaped whitespace in a value**: an **escape is opaque** ‚Äî nothing inside it is structure. `\` followed by a space is a valid CSS escape whose escaped code point **is that space** (CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß4.3.4 "Check if two code points are a valid escape" ‚Äî only a newline after `\` invalidates it ‚Äî and ¬ß4.3.7 "Consume an escaped code point", whose final branch returns the code point itself). So the trailing space in `width: 50px\ ;` is value *content*, not padding: the value is the ident `50px `, and the `;` terminates the declaration. tsv preserves every escape whole; prettier scans through them and corrupts each kind differently:

- **Trailing payload dropped, delimiter stranded** ‚Äî `width: 50px\ ;` ‚Üí `width: 50px\;`, `var(--a, 50px\ )` ‚Üí `var(--a, 50px\)`, `calc(1px\ )` ‚Üí `calc(1px\)`. The `;` / `)` becomes an *escaped* character, so the declaration, the function, and the block never close: **prettier's own output no longer re-parses** (tsv's CSS parser rejects it with `Expected '}'`).
- **Payload dropped mid-value** ‚Äî `color: a\ b` ‚Üí `color: a\b`, silently changing the value from `a b` to `ab`.
- **Escaped delimiter read as structure** ‚Äî `var(--b, x\,y)` ‚Üí `var(--b, x\, y)` (the escaped comma splits one ident, which the comma path rejoins with `", "`) and `inset: a\+b` ‚Üí `inset: a\+ b` (the escaped `+` takes operator spacing). Both split a single ident into two values.
- **Wrapping inside an ident** ‚Äî a long value may break *on* an escaped space, putting a `\` at end-of-line; `\` before a newline is not a valid escape at all. See [escaped_whitespace_long](../tests/fixtures/css/values/escaped_whitespace_long_prettier_divergence/), which pins the 100/101 boundary.

A **hex** escape is opaque for one byte more than it looks: it takes up to six hex digits and then, optionally, **one whitespace terminator**, which belongs to the escape (¬ß4.3.7). `\41 2px` is therefore the single ident `A2px`, not `\41` followed by `2px` ‚Äî here prettier agrees, pinned by the regular fixture [escaped_hex_terminator](../tests/fixtures/css/values/escaped_hex_terminator/).

An unquoted `url()` has the same failure at its closing paren ‚Äî `url(x\ )` ‚Üí `url(x\)`, and the url token then never terminates ‚Äî pinned separately by [url_escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/url_escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/), since url content is opaque and takes its own code path.

tsv declines to reproduce any of it ‚Äî its format‚Üíre-parse invariant outranks matching prettier, and emitting output that does not parse is never the defensible side. Svelte's error-recovering `parseCss` still consumes prettier's output, so this is a *formatter* divergence only; tsv's parse AST matches `parseCss` on the input exactly. The selector axis (an escaped space before a combinator, `,`, or `{`, on a class/id/type leaf **or a pseudo**) is a plain bug rather than a divergence ‚Äî prettier gets it right ‚Äî and is pinned by [css/selectors/escaped_names](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/escaped_names/); so is the whitespace-collapse inside a dropped forgiving-selector item ([forgiving_is_where](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/forgiving_is_where_svelte_divergence/)). See [escaped_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/css/values/escaped_whitespace_prettier_divergence/).

**String glued to a non-ASCII space**: A comma- or space-separated value whose element is a quoted string glued to a **non-ASCII whitespace** character ‚Äî a non-breaking space (U+00A0) or an em space (U+2003) ‚Äî on either side, as in `grid-template-areas: 'x', <NBSP>'y'` (leading) or `grid-template-columns: 'a'<NBSP>, 'b'` (trailing). CSS whitespace is ASCII-only (CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß4.2), so a non-ASCII space is not a separator but value content ‚Äî tsv treats every code point ‚â• U+00A0 as an identifier code point, following Svelte's `parseCss` (broader than the CSS Syntax ident set, which excludes these look-alike whitespace chars). tsv keeps the element as **one opaque token, inline**, preserving the character. Prettier's value tokenizer splits it into a word (`<NBSP>`) plus a string (`'y'`), which makes the group multi-token ‚Äî so prettier inserts a space between them and, for a comma list, breaks it one item per line (`<NBSP> 'y'`). tsv does not split adjacent glued value tokens, so the run stays one token and its bytes survive verbatim ‚Äî the same lossless form it emits for the pure-ASCII analog `font-family: 'x', a'y'` (tsv keeps `a'y'`; prettier splits to `a 'y'`). This pins a former **content loss**: the value parser's element-boundary trims and the printer's value-text whitespace normalizer both used the Unicode-aware `str::trim`, which drops a boundary non-ASCII space ‚Äî for a string element outright (the narrowed text no longer began with a quote, so the string printer emitted nothing and the whole element vanished, `'x',;` then `'x';` on a second pass ‚Äî non-idempotent). The fix trims only CSS whitespace (`trim_start_css` / `trim_end_preserving_escape`, the same escape-aware trims that keep an escaped `50px\ ` whole), matching CSS's ASCII-only definition. See [comma_string_nonascii_space](../tests/fixtures/css/values/lists/comma_string_nonascii_space_prettier_divergence/).

**Single value glued to a non-ASCII space**: The single-value (non-list) sibling of the above. A **single** declaration value glued to a non-ASCII whitespace character ‚Äî a non-breaking space (U+00A0) or an em space (U+2003) ‚Äî at either boundary, as in `content: <NBSP>'z'` (leading) or `quotes: 'a'<NBSP>` (trailing). Same rule and same design choice: the non-ASCII space is value content ‚Äî tsv treats it as an identifier code point (‚â• U+00A0), following Svelte's `parseCss` ‚Äî so tsv keeps the value as **one opaque token, inline** (`content: <NBSP>'z'`), while prettier splits a **string** value into a word (`<NBSP>`) plus the string and inserts a space (`content: <NBSP> 'z'`). For an **identifier** value (`font-family: <NBSP>q`) prettier keeps it glued, so tsv matches prettier there ‚Äî only the string cases diverge. This pins a former **content loss** (the space was dropped, `content: <NBSP>'z'` ‚Üí `content: 'z'`): a **trailing** space was stripped by `locate_value`'s Unicode-aware value-boundary trim (now CSS-whitespace-only via the escape-aware `trim_start_css` / `trim_end_preserving_escape`), and a **leading** space was skipped by the lexer's `char::is_whitespace()` whitespace scan as part of the colon‚Üívalue gap before the value began (the scan now treats only ASCII whitespace as CSS whitespace, per CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß4.2, so a code point ‚â• U+00A0 ‚Äî which `parseCss` treats as an identifier code point ‚Äî is no longer skipped). See [boundary_nonascii_space](../tests/fixtures/css/values/boundary_nonascii_space_prettier_divergence/).

**Glued run of quoted strings**: The pure-ASCII sibling of the two glued cases above, with no separator at all. A single declaration value that is a **run of glued value tokens** whose first and last token are quoted strings, written adjacent: `content: 'a''b'` (two strings), `content: 'a'x'b'` (string, ident, string), `content: "a"x"b"` (double-quoted). tsv does not split adjacent glued value tokens, so it keeps the run as **one opaque token, inline**, verbatim (`content: 'a'x'b'`); prettier's tokenizer splits it into its component tokens and inserts a space, also normalizing the quote (`content: 'a' x 'b'`). Same lossless choice as `font-family: 'x', a'y'` (tsv keeps `a'y'`; prettier splits to `a 'y'`). This pins a former **content corruption**: the value re-parser's `parse_string_literal` classified the run as a single string on "first char is a quote and last char is the matching quote" ‚Äî true for `'a'x'b'` even though its opening `'` closes at index 2 ‚Äî then stripped the outer quotes and re-quoted the interior, turning the **delimiter** quotes into literal content (`content: 'a'x'b'` ‚Üí `content: "a'x'b"`, a value whose CSS meaning changed and which round-trips to a different AST). The fix requires the opening quote's first **unescaped** matching close to fall at the end of the run (`quoted_string_spans_all`); otherwise the run is kept verbatim as an opaque identifier. An escaped interior quote (`'a\'b'`) still closes at the end, so a genuine single string is unaffected. See [glued_string_run](../tests/fixtures/css/values/glued_string_run_prettier_divergence/).

**Escaped-paren url() whitespace**: An unquoted `url(...)` whose content carries an escaped paren (`\(` / `\)`) and outer whitespace inside the parens. Per CSS Syntax 3 ¬ß4.3.6 the `<url-token>` tokenizer consumes the leading/trailing whitespace, so its canonical value is trimmed; tsv emits that form (`url(  a\(b  )` ‚Üí `url(a\(b)`). Prettier trims plain url whitespace the same way, but its postcss escaped-paren handling ‚Äî the same bug that makes it *throw* on [url_escaped_paren](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/url_escaped_paren_prettier_divergence/) (`url(a\)b)` ‚Üí `Unbalanced parenthesis`) ‚Äî here stops normalizing and keeps the whitespace verbatim (`url(  a\(b  )` stays as-is). Prettier's output is valid, but tsv follows the spec's canonical serialization, so the divergence is escaped-paren-only (plain content agrees). Because tsv's trimmed form is dual-stable, this is pinned by a `prettier_variant_*` rather than an `output_prettier`. On Prettier's own corpus it surfaces in `tests/format/css/url/url.css`. See [url_escaped_paren_ws](../tests/fixtures/css/values/functions/url_escaped_paren_ws_prettier_divergence/).

### CSS: Layout

**Greedy fill overflow** (‚óÜprint_width) ‚Äî [comma_separated_greedy_fill](../tests/fixtures/css/values/lists/comma_separated_greedy_fill_prettier_divergence/): Prettier's `fill()` algorithm allows lines to exceed `printWidth` by 1 char when fill segments exactly consume remaining width and the parent adds trailing punctuation. tsv treats `printWidth` as a hard limit.

> **Related fill boundary divergences**: Several fixtures test variations of Prettier allowing lines to exceed `printWidth`. These share a common root cause‚ÄîPrettier's `fill()` algorithm boundary conditions:
>
> - CSS: `comma_space_separated_long`, `comma_separated_greedy_fill`
> - Svelte: `inline_element_fill_long`, `inline_component_fill_long`, `fill_after_inline`, `block_multiline_attrs_content_hug`, `multiline_value_inline_long`, `fill_expr_break_boundary_long`
> - TypeScript: `long` (template literals)

### CSS: Comments

**‚óÜstable_quirk** (except where a per-entry reason is noted). Prettier has stable variants for comment positioning. tsv normalizes consistently.

- At-rule before `{` ‚Äî [atrule_before_opening_brace](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/atrule_before_opening_brace_prettier_divergence/)
- At-rule in prelude ‚Äî [atrule_in_prelude](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/atrule_in_prelude_prettier_divergence/)
- After colon in values ‚Äî [in_property_value_after_colon](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/in_property_value_after_colon_prettier_divergence/)
- Before colon in values ‚Äî [in_property_value_before_colon](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/in_property_value_before_colon_prettier_divergence/)
- Before colon, two or more comments (the property‚Üícolon gap is the only place a CSS declaration comment survives, so every comment is preserved, joined single-spaced ‚Äî reconstructing only the first is silent content loss) ‚Äî [multi_comment_before_colon](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/multi_comment_before_colon_prettier_divergence/)
- Before colon, comment contains a colon (scan robustness) ‚Äî [colon_in_property_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/colon_in_property_comment_prettier_divergence/)
- @media prelude ‚Äî [media_list](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/media_list_prettier_divergence/)
- @media long with `/* */` ‚Äî Print width (the comment is incidental; the divergence is the over-width unwrapped query) ‚Äî [media_long](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/media_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Selector before `{` ‚Äî [selector_before_opening_brace](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/selector_before_opening_brace_prettier_divergence/)
- Selector before `{` (‚â•2) ‚Äî [selector_before_opening_brace_multiple](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/selector_before_opening_brace_multiple_prettier_divergence/)
- Selector before `{` (in at-rule) ‚Äî [selector_before_opening_brace_in_atrule](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/selector_before_opening_brace_in_atrule_prettier_divergence/)
- Selector list ‚Äî [selector_list](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/selector_list_prettier_divergence/)
- Selector list (nested `:is()` / before-comma) ‚Äî [selector_nested_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/selector_nested_comment_prettier_divergence/)
- Multi-line comment in gaps (comma / before `{` / value) ‚Äî the comment interior stays verbatim (continuation lines keep their authored column, never reindented by the `<style>` embedding); tsv joins the gap single-spaced while prettier preserves the authored layout (an own-line comment stays own-line) ‚Äî [multi_line_gap](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/comments/multi_line_gap_prettier_divergence/)
- :nth-\*() arg gaps (before the An+B, around `of`, after the `of` list) ‚Äî [nth_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_class/nth_comment_svelte_prettier_divergence/): gap comments normalize to single-space separation; a comment **inside** the An+B expression text freezes the An+B verbatim (no operator respacing ‚Äî it would corrupt comment content), matching prettier, which also skips An+B normalization when a comment is present
- Combinator boundaries (descendant / child / sibling / column gap, before or after the symbol, and a `:has()` relative-selector leading combinator) ‚Äî the gap comment normalizes to single-space separation, the same rule as the other selector-comment positions; a glued compound-internal comment (`.a/* c */.b`) stays glued (adding a space would turn the compound into a descendant `.a .b`). Prettier freezes the source whitespace verbatim. Svelte's `parseCss` rejects these outright (`css_expected_identifier`), so this is also a `_svelte_divergence` ‚Äî see [conformance_svelte.md](./conformance_svelte.md#css-corrections). ‚Äî [combinator_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/combinator_comment_svelte_prettier_divergence/)
- Glued comment run in a compound (`.a/* c *//* d */.b`) ‚Äî the run stays a compound and is emitted verbatim (no space inserted between the two comments ‚Äî that would tokenize as whitespace and make it a descendant); prettier agrees it's a compound but stably relocates the opening `{` onto its own line (a cosmetic quirk ‚Äî prettier's output is convergent, valid, and meaning-preserving, so it stays under the section's `‚óÜstable_quirk`, not `‚óÜprettier_bug`). Svelte's `parseCss` rejects it (`css_expected_identifier`), so also a `_svelte_divergence`. ‚Äî [compound_comment_run](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/compound_comment_run_svelte_prettier_divergence/)
- Pseudo-arg gaps (`::slotted()` compound / `::part()` idents / `:dir()`/`:lang()`/`::highlight()` / an unrecognized functional pseudo-class's selector arg) ‚Äî leading/trailing comments normalize to single-space separation, the same rule as the other selector-comment positions. For `::part()` the *interior* gaps between two part names normalize the same way ‚Äî a comment there reads as whitespace and is rejected by parseCss (`css_expected_identifier`), so it is a `_svelte_prettier_divergence` (part_interior_comment). `::slotted()`'s arg parses as a complex-selector-list, so an interior comment (between compounds, or glued compound-internal) is a combinator-boundary case handled by the shared selector machinery (see combinator_comment), not a `::slotted`-specific rule. The `:dir()`/`:lang()`/`::highlight()` and unrecognized-pseudo args parse as ordinary selector lists (Svelte's model), so their gap comments interleave exactly like `:is()`'s; the single-value cases here lead or trail the value. ‚Äî [slotted_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_element/slotted_comment_prettier_divergence/), [part_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_element/part_comment_prettier_divergence/), [part_interior_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_element/part_interior_comment_svelte_prettier_divergence/), [dir_lang_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_class/dir_lang_comment_prettier_divergence/), [highlight_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_element/highlight_comment_prettier_divergence/), [unknown_arg_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/selectors/pseudo_class/unknown_arg_comment_prettier_divergence/)
- `@scope` prelude selector lists ‚Äî a comment leading or trailing the root or limit selector list (`@scope (/* c */ .a) to (.b /* c */)`) normalizes to single-space separation, the same rule as the `:is()` argument gaps: `@scope`'s clauses parse through the identical complex-selector-list path. Prettier freezes the source whitespace instead. parseCss accepts these and strips the comment from the wire `prelude` string (`( .a) to (.b )`), so this is prettier-only (not a `_svelte_divergence`). ‚Äî [scope_selector_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scope_selector_comment_prettier_divergence/)
- `@scope` prelude structural gaps (the out-of-paren counterpart of the above) ‚Äî a comment leading the prelude (`@scope /* c */ (.a)`), between the root clause and `to` (`@scope (.a) /* c */ to (.b)`), between `to` and the limit clause (`@scope to /* c */ (.b)`), or after the last clause before the block `{` (`@scope (.a) /* c */ {`) normalizes to single-space separation on each side, the same rule as the in-paren case. Prettier freezes the source whitespace (inserting only a space after the `@scope` name and collapsing the pre-`{` run). parseCss accepts these and drops the comment from the wire (leading/pre-`{` comments sit outside the prelude span; between/after-`to` comments strip in place, leaving the whitespace ‚Äî `(.a)  to (.b)`), so this is prettier-only. ‚Äî [scope_prelude_gap_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/at_rules/scope_prelude_gap_comment_prettier_divergence/)

### CSS: HTML comments (CDO/CDC)

**‚óÜprettier_bug.** Legacy `<!-- ‚Ä¶ -->` HTML-comment markers in CSS ‚Äî the CDO/CDC tokens from the old `<style><!-- ‚Ä¶ --></style>` browser-hiding idiom. Prettier can't format them: rather than throwing, it mangles the markers into invalid CSS (`<!-- -->` ‚Üí `<!-- -- >`, splitting the `-->` and gluing the next line), so there is no prettier oracle. tsv follows Svelte's `parseCss`, which reads `<!--` ‚Ä¶ `-->` as a comment span and **discards** it ‚Äî including any wrapped CSS ‚Äî so the markers (and their contents) drop on format. Svelte's swallow itself departs from the CSS Syntax spec, where `<!--` (CDO) and `-->` (CDC) are independent no-op tokens and the content between them survives (so the spec ‚Äî and, mangling aside, prettier ‚Äî keep a wrapped rule; `parseCss`, and thus tsv, drop it). tsv inherits `parseCss` behavior by design, not the spec's token rules. The parse side (which positions swallow, which keep the markers raw, unterminated errors) is pinned in [conformance_svelte.md ¬ßCSS Compat Behaviors](./conformance_svelte.md#css-compat-behaviors) and [tests/css_cdo_cdc.rs](../tests/css_cdo_cdc.rs).

- HTML comment markers drop on format ‚Äî [html_comment](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/html_comment_prettier_divergence/)

### Whitespace: BOM Handling

**‚óÜbom_stripping.** Prettier preserves byte-order marks. tsv strips them (they serve no purpose in UTF-8).

- Svelte ‚Äî [bom](../tests/fixtures/svelte/syntax/whitespace/bom_prettier_divergence/)
- CSS ‚Äî [bom](../tests/fixtures/css/tokens/whitespace/bom_prettier_divergence/)
- TypeScript ‚Äî [bom](../tests/fixtures/typescript/syntax/whitespace/bom_prettier_divergence/)

### Svelte: Elements

- Menu block element ‚Äî ‚óÜspec_violation ‚Äî [menu_block](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/menu_block_prettier_divergence/)
- Self-closing non-void ‚Äî ‚óÜspec_precedence ‚Äî [self_closing_nonvoid](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/self_closing_nonvoid_prettier_divergence/), [ws_sensitive_self_closing_kinds](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/ws_sensitive_self_closing_kinds_prettier_divergence/) (the same rule inside `<pre>`/`<textarea>`: kept for component/foreign/namespaced, normalized for plain HTML ‚Äî whitespace-sensitivity governs content, not tag serialization) ‚Äî self-closing tags **don't exist in HTML**: a `/` before `>` on a non-void, non-foreign start tag is the `non-void-html-element-start-tag-with-trailing-solidus` parse error and "the parser behaves as if the U+002F (/) is not present" (so `<div/><span></span>` nests the span *inside* the div). Svelte's parser instead reads it as self-closing, making the authored form mean different things to different readers; tsv emits the form that means the same thing to both. tsv allows `/` exactly where the spec gives it meaning ‚Äî foreign content (SVG/MathML), namespaced elements, void elements (no-op) ‚Äî plus components, which aren't HTML elements
- Fill after inline ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [fill_after_inline](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_after_inline_prettier_divergence/)
- Fill boundary ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [inline_element_fill_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_element_fill_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Fill after breaking attr ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [multiline_value_inline_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/multiline_value_inline_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Component fill boundary ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [inline_component_fill_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_component_fill_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Wide inline child own-line ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [inline_component_wide_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_component_wide_long_prettier_divergence/) (component), [inline_component_wide_longname_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_component_wide_longname_long_prettier_divergence/) (long tag name), [inline_component_wide_multi_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_component_wide_multi_long_prettier_divergence/) (two components), [inline_component_wide_multiattr_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_component_wide_multiattr_long_prettier_divergence/) (multi-attr, breakable inner), [inline_svelte_element_wide_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_svelte_element_wide_long_prettier_divergence/) (special element), [inline_element_wide_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_element_wide_long_prettier_divergence/) (HTML element parity), [inline_element_wide_multiattr_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_element_wide_multiattr_long_prettier_divergence/) (HTML element multi-attr drop coupling)
- Wide inline content + trailing text ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [inline_wide_content_trailing_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_wide_content_trailing_long_prettier_divergence/) (wide content lays out **block-style** with both tags intact; space-authored trailing text hugs the intact `</tag>`; `<strong>` + `<a>`), [inline_wide_content_trailing_sandwiched_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_wide_content_trailing_sandwiched_long_prettier_divergence/) (same, but the wide element is **sandwiched** by a preceding text sibling ‚Äî the terminal tail still hugs, since nothing follows it), [inline_wide_content_trailing_newline_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_wide_content_trailing_newline_long_prettier_divergence/) (newline-authored trailing text keeps its own line), [inline_wide_content_text_sibling_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_wide_content_text_sibling_long_prettier_divergence/) (non-terminal text before a following element keeps its own line), [inline_nested_child_trailing_space_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_nested_child_trailing_space_long_prettier_divergence/) (nested wide child + trailing text: dual-stable ‚Äî newline boundary keeps own line, space boundary hugs `</tag>`; both forms stable under tsv and prettier), [inline_short_content_fill_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_short_content_fill_long_prettier_divergence/) (the **short-element** counterpart: a short inline element sandwiched in a wrapping fill packs greedily and pairwise after the preceding word rather than being isolated onto its own line; the print_width wrap is the sole divergence), [inline_short_component_fill_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_short_component_fill_long_prettier_divergence/) (the **component** sibling of the above ‚Äî a short inline *component* packs pairwise identically, since both route through the same element-type-agnostic after-element fold). See [¬ßSvelte: Inline content block-style](#svelte-inline-content-block-style).
- Inline closing intact ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [inline_closing_intact_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_closing_intact_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Fill multiple expr ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [fill_multiple_expr_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_multiple_expr_long_prettier_divergence/) (one breakable expression, which must break), [fill_competing_expr](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_competing_expr_prettier_divergence/) (**two** breakable expressions, only one of which needs to ‚Äî tsv breaks the first at its `?`, prettier the second at its `!==` and overshoots to 102; the choice must also be *stable*, since a padded content boundary that strands those groups flat makes the two layouts alternate forever)
- Inline content (text) ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [inline_content_text_wrap](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_content_text_wrap_prettier_divergence/), [text_non_breaking_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/text_non_breaking_whitespace_prettier_divergence/) ‚Äî an inline element's wrapping text content lays out **block-style** (both tags intact, content on its own indented line, collapsing inline when it fits); prettier pre-breaks the opening tag. See [¬ßSvelte: Inline content block-style](#svelte-inline-content-block-style).
- Inline content (expression) ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [inline_content_hug_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_content_hug_long_prettier_divergence/) ‚Äî breakable-expression content also lays out **block-style** (uniform with text/element content), where prettier dangles. See [¬ßSvelte: Inline content block-style](#svelte-inline-content-block-style).
- Inline content (spaced expression tags) ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [inline_content_spaced_tags_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_content_spaced_tags_long_prettier_divergence/) ‚Äî space-separated expression tags (`{a} {b}`) each take their own line once the element goes block-style, where prettier dangles the compact authoring and lets it run past printWidth. See [¬ßSvelte: Inline content block-style](#svelte-inline-content-block-style).
- Block multiline attrs hug ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [block_multiline_attrs_content_hug](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/block_multiline_attrs_content_hug_prettier_divergence/)
- Fill expr break boundary ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [fill_expr_break_boundary_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_expr_break_boundary_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Fill break before expr ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [fill_break_before_expr_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_break_before_expr_long_prettier_divergence/) (overflowing fill whose continuation begins with an `{expression}` tag: tsv breaks _before_ the tag to hold the line ‚â§ 100 ‚Äî the tag leads the continuation with no leading space ‚Äî where prettier keeps it on the line at 101; the break must be stable, so the collapsible space in front of the tag is consumed by the line break rather than stranded at the head of the continuation)
- Fill tail after expr ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [fill_tail_after_expr_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_tail_after_expr_long_prettier_divergence/) (the same parity shift where the text is the element's **last** child, so the fill's final `[line, word]` pair is the one that overflows: tsv breaks at the collapsible space before the tail word, prettier keeps it and overflows to 101; prettier is stable on both authorings, so the divergence is one of normalization)
- Fill tail multiword ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [fill_tail_multiword_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_tail_multiword_long_prettier_divergence/) (the parity-shifted tail with more than one word: the break lands at the FIRST separator that overflows, taking the whole tail to the continuation line, where prettier keeps it at 101)
- Fill tail before sibling ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [fill_tail_before_sibling_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_tail_before_sibling_long_prettier_divergence/) (tail text followed by an inline sibling, so the fill carries BOTH a leading and a trailing separator and crosses both halves of the parity rule at once)
- Fill tail wide char ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [fill_tail_wide_char_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_tail_wide_char_long_prettier_divergence/) (the parity-shifted tail with a CJK tail word, pinning that the break measures VISUAL width ‚Äî the glyph is 2 columns, so the 100/101 pair fails if it is ever counted as 1)
- @debug comments ‚Äî ‚óÜcontent_preservation ‚Äî [debug_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/tags/debug/debug_comment_prettier_divergence/), [debug_multiline_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/tags/debug/debug_multiline_comment_prettier_divergence/) (a multi-line block reindents to context like everywhere else), [debug_comma_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/tags/debug/debug_comma_comment_prettier_divergence/) (the inter-item positions on both sides of the comma ‚Äî a comment before the comma trails the previous identifier, one after it leads the next)
- svelte:element `this` ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [svelte_element_this_string](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/svelte_element_this_string_prettier_divergence/). Anything between the `{` and a string literal (a paren, or a leading comment) fails prettier's `{`-precedes-literal check and collapses the binding to the plain attribute `this="x"` ‚Äî which for a comment is also ‚óÜcontent_preservation, since the collapsed form has nowhere to put it and prettier drops it.
- svelte:element class ws ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [svelte_element_class_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/svelte_element_class_whitespace_prettier_divergence/)
- Space after block element ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [space_after_block](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/space_after_block_prettier_divergence/)

**Fill after inline**: Prettier's fill algorithm allows lines to exceed print width when text follows an inline element closing tag. Prettier produces 111 char lines, tsv breaks at exactly 100 chars.

**Fill boundary**: When fill content exceeds print width, Prettier tolerates the overage while tsv breaks earlier. This is an emergent behavior from prettier-plugin-svelte's doc structure (separate fills per text node with `group([line, element])` wrappers). See also `inline_element_fill_100/` which shows both formatters match at exactly 100 chars.

**Fill after breaking attr**: When an inline element has breaking attributes (e.g., multiline values) and long trailing text follows, Prettier's `handleTextChild` early return for last-child text skips wrapping the previous element, so there's no break point between the closing tag and trailing text. Prettier allows the line to exceed print width (102 chars). tsv's fill correctly breaks trailing words at the print width boundary (100 chars). See also `multiline_value_inline/` which shows both formatters match when trailing text is short.

**Component fill boundary**: Same fill boundary behavior as above but with component elements (`<Comp>text</Comp>`) instead of HTML inline elements. At 101 chars, Prettier keeps everything on one line while tsv breaks the closing `>` of the closing tag to stay within print width. At 100 chars both formatters match.
