**Wide inline child own-line**: When an inline child (component or HTML element) is too wide to share a line with the preceding text, Prettier hugs it onto the text line (101+) and breaks it internally ‚Äî attributes wrap and the closing `>` dangles (the inline content hug). tsv keeps printWidth a hard limit, so the whole child drops to its own line and the preceding word stays hugged on the text line. The break sits at the collapsible space before the child, so it holds regardless of tag-name length (`inline_component_wide_longname_long`), for repeated children in one run (`inline_component_wide_multi_long`), for a multi-attribute component whose own attributes could break (`inline_component_wide_multiattr_long` ‚Äî it still drops whole, attributes intact), and for special elements (`inline_svelte_element_wide_long`); HTML inline elements produce the identical shape (`inline_element_wide_long`, and `inline_element_wide_multiattr_long` for the multi-attribute counterpart). When a *short* dropped child (its content fits, so the whole tag stays intact on its own line) is followed by trailing text, that text follows the **authored boundary** exactly like the wide-content case below ‚Äî a space flows after the intact tag, a newline keeps its own line ‚Äî because the short child packs its tail like any other fill word (`inline_component_wide_multiattr_long` / `inline_element_wide_multiattr_long`). These fixtures also pin idempotence ‚Äî the compact authored form and Prettier's hugged form both normalize to the flow form in one pass.

**Wide inline content + trailing text**: The mirror of the above for an element whose own _content_ (not its attributes) overflows, followed by trailing text ‚Äî `<strong>‚Ä¶90 chars‚Ä¶</strong> tail`. Prettier keeps the content on a single over-width line and lets `>‚Ä¶content‚Ä¶</tag` exceed printWidth (the inline content hug again); tsv wraps the content _inside_ the element, so every line stays ‚â§100. The trailing text's placement follows the **authored boundary**: a space hugs the intact `</tag>` (`</tag> tail` ‚Äî `inline_wide_content_trailing_long`, covering both `<strong>` with no attributes and `<a>` with a short one), a newline keeps it on its own line (`inline_wide_content_trailing_newline_long`). This mirrors how a _short_ inline element already keeps `<el>x</el> tail` inline for a space and breaks for a newline ‚Äî tsv treats the boundary whitespace before trailing text as a meaningful authoring choice rather than normalizing it away. Prettier's tail placement is the same on both forms (space hugs, newline breaks), so the **content wrap is the sole divergence** on each. The `unformatted_ours_*` variants pin tsv's idempotence: differently-authored space forms all normalize to the hugged form in one pass. A non-terminal text run (followed by another inline element) instead keeps its own line regardless of authoring ‚Äî hugging it is non-convergent (`inline_wide_content_text_sibling_long`). The terminal-hug is scoped to *terminal* trailing text, **not** to a first-child element: a wide element **sandwiched** by a preceding text sibling (pushed to its own line by a preceding break) still lets its space-authored terminal tail hug the intact `</tag>` (`inline_wide_content_trailing_sandwiched_long`) ‚Äî nothing follows the tail, so the hug stays convergent. This boundary-respecting choice also covers the **dropped short child**: a short element pushed to its own line by the preceding text (`inline_component_wide_multiattr_long` / `inline_element_wide_multiattr_long`) packs its space-authored tail after the intact tag and keeps a newline tail on its own line, just like the wide-content case. It does not yet apply uniformly to the nested wide child (`inline_nested_child_trailing_space_long`), which is dual-stable (a newline boundary keeps its own line, a space boundary hugs `</tag>`).

Separately, a **short** inline element sandwiched in a wrapping fill packs *pairwise* into the surrounding fill after the preceding word rather than being isolated onto its own line (`inline_short_content_fill_long`, HTML `<code>`; `inline_short_component_fill_long`, the component sibling): the flow boundary measures whether the *element* fits after the preceding word ‚Äî mirroring prettier's greedy fill ‚Äî not the whole element-plus-trailing-text unit. When the packed run exceeds printWidth tsv wraps it at a word boundary where prettier keeps the over-width inline-content hug, which is the sole divergence. Components and HTML inline elements pack identically because the fold (`build_after_element_fold`) takes a plain `DocId` and never inspects the element's type.

**Fill expr break boundary**: When fill content includes a multiline expression (e.g., binary `+` that breaks across lines), subsequent text continues on the continuation line. At the width boundary, Prettier allows the continuation line to reach 101 chars while tsv breaks at 96 to stay under 100. See also `fill_expr_break_continuation_long/` for matching behavior when continuation stays under 100.

**Fill multiple expr**: When fill mode content has multiple expression tags with ternaries, Prettier breaks the opening bracket and packs more onto a single line (101 chars), breaking within the comparison operator (`!==`). tsv keeps the opening bracket hugging content and breaks earlier at the first ternary operator (`?`) to stay within 100 chars (max 79). When **two** expressions are breakable and only one of them *needs* to break ([fill_competing_expr](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/fill_competing_expr_prettier_divergence/)), tsv breaks the first and leaves the second flat ‚Äî and that choice must be *stable*: the expression groups stay breakable on the padded-boundary path too, or the fill's `line` separators short-circuit the width check of the group before them, a different expression is left flat each pass, and the two layouts alternate forever.

**Inline content (expression)**: When inline element content with _breakable_ expressions (ternaries, `&&`/`||`, `+`/`-`) exceeds print width, tsv lays it out **block-style** ‚Äî both tags intact, the content on its own indented line, where the expression usually fits unbroken (and wraps within printWidth only if still too wide). Prettier instead dangles the tag delimiters and breaks the expression operator-by-operator at the tighter dangled indent. This is uniform with text and element content; see ¬ßSvelte: Inline content block-style.

**Menu block element**: prettier-plugin-svelte's `blockElements` list includes `ol` and `ul` but omits `menu`. The HTML spec treats `<menu>` identically to `<ul>` ‚Äî same `display: block`, same CSS rules (`padding-inline-start: 40px`, `counter-reset: list-item`). The spec explicitly says: _"The `menu` element is simply a semantic alternative to `ul`."_ tsv includes `<menu>` in the block element list (spec-compliant), causing block formatting (expanded content) where Prettier hugs content. This only manifests when compact input is formatted ‚Äî both formatters preserve the block form if given it directly.

**Block multiline attrs hug**: When whitespace-sensitive elements (`<pre>`, `<textarea>`) have multiline attributes and hugged content that would exceed print width, Prettier keeps `>{content}</tag>` on the attribute line (101+ chars). tsv breaks `>` to its own line (`\n>{content}`) to respect print width while preserving whitespace semantics (no text node added since `>` immediately precedes content).

**svelte:element `this`**: prettier-plugin-svelte ignores `singleQuote` for a brace-wrapped string literal in `<svelte:element this={‚Ä¶}>`, always emitting double quotes (`this={'hello'}` ‚Üí `this={"hello"}`), and skips escaping entirely ‚Äî so `this={'a"b'}` becomes the invalid `this={"a"b"}` and `this={'a\b'}` corrupts to a backspace. tsv delegates the literal to the normal string printer, honoring `singleQuote` and escaping like any other string. The bug is narrow ‚Äî only a *directly* brace-wrapped string literal triggers it; concatenations, template literals, and other expressions delegate to the JS printer and agree (boundary fixture [svelte_element_this](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/svelte_element_this/)). One adjacent facet diverges further: a *parenthesized* literal `this={('hello')}` collapses to the plain attribute `this="hello"` under prettier (structural rewrite), while tsv keeps `this={'hello'}` ‚Äî encoded by the fixture's `unformatted_ours_paren` + `variant_paren_collapse` pair.

**svelte:element class ws**: prettier-plugin-svelte does not collapse repeated whitespace in a `class` attribute on `<svelte:element>` (`class="a   b    c"` stays verbatim), while it still collapses on a plain element (`<div class="a   b    c">` ‚Üí `class="a b c"`) ‚Äî and so does tsv, everywhere. The `<svelte:element>` attribute path runs off a separate code path from the normal attribute printer, like the `this` bug. tsv collapses uniformly across all elements. Both formatters keep the single-spaced form stable; the divergence shows only when collapsing multi-space input.

**Space after block element**: When a block element (`<div>`, `<p>`, ‚Ä¶) is directly followed by content text with a same-line (space, no linebreak) boundary, prettier-plugin-svelte trims the text's leading whitespace (`trimTextNodeLeft`) but still emits the block-child break, stranding a **leading space** on the text line (`<div>block</div> text` ‚Üí `>‚èé text`). It is **non-idempotent** ‚Äî a second pass trims the space, converging to the same form tsv produces. tsv takes the same trim but emits no fold/group after the block (the block's own break already supplies the separating line), so no stray space survives and the result is identical in one pass from either authoring. The `unformatted_ours_compact` variant pins tsv's one-pass normalization; `prettier_intermediate_compact` captures prettier's stray-space first pass (which converges to `input` on the next pass).

### Svelte: Inline content block-style

Design choice. tsv lays out an inline element's **wrapping content** block-style ‚Äî both tags stay intact and the content moves to its own indented line(s), collapsing to `<tag>content</tag>` when it fits, exactly like a block element. Prettier instead **dangles** the tag delimiters (`<tag‚èé\t>content</tag‚èé>`, pre-breaking the opening tag and dangling the closing `>`). This is uniform across text, expression, and element/component children, with and without attributes (the `>` is **attr-keyed** ‚Äî it hugs the last attribute when attributes fit and dedents to its own line when they wrap), and including table cells (which are inline-classified). Content that fits stays inline; only overflow breaks to block-style.

Content-boundary whitespace is **render-free under Svelte 5** ‚Äî start/end-of-content whitespace is trimmed at compile (`<p>foo<span> - bar</span></p>` renders `foo- bar`), so the injected block-style boundaries are render-equivalent (confirmed at corpus scale by `ast_diff --render`).

Because it is render-free, that whitespace does **not select the layout**. Wherever the content goes multiline, the rule holds without exception: it holds whether the content breaks **structurally** (a block child, a control-flow block) or by **width**, and it holds for a boundary the author *hugged* (zero whitespace) exactly as for one they spaced or broke. So the authorings of one document ‚Äî `<span>text<div>‚Ä¶`, `<span> text<div>‚Ä¶`, and the newline form ‚Äî converge on one form. Prettier lets the boundary decide, so it keeps a *different* stable form for each ([content_boundary_convergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/content_boundary_convergence_prettier_divergence/) is one document with three prettier forms and one tsv form), and its space form is additionally **non-idempotent** (the space is emitted at line-start, where the next parse reads it as indentation and drops it). This is the authoring-independence property `authoring_audit` checks ‚Äî it mutates each content boundary across hug ‚Üî space ‚Üî newline and requires every authoring to converge.

The corollary is that whitespace *inside* the content ‚Äî a **separator between two siblings** ‚Äî is render-significant and therefore does still decide layout. Whitespace between two adjacent expression tags (`{a} {b}`) is a collapsible break: a space while the element fits, a newline once it goes block-style, so each tag takes its own line ([inline_content_spaced_tags_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_content_spaced_tags_long_prettier_divergence/)); a text run between them flows as one fill and keeps them on the content line. The boundary carries no signal and must not select the layout; the separator carries one and must.

**Scope: every fragment in the language, not just an element's content.** Svelte has two families of fragments ‚Äî an element's/component's content, and **block bodies** (`{#if}` / `{:else}` / `{#each}` and its `{:else}` fallback / `{#key}` / each `{#await}` phase / `{#snippet}`) ‚Äî and their boundaries are **equally render-free** (verified against `svelte/compiler`: every fragment boundary in the language is trimmed at compile; only inter-sibling whitespace and `<pre>`/`<textarea>` are significant). The stance applies to both: a block whose body renders multiline lays out block-style ‚Äî head and tail intact, body on its own indented lines ‚Äî however the author wrote that boundary, collapsing inline when the body fits. Prettier instead lets the boundary decide, keeping a hugged body hugged (`{#if c}<div>b1</div>‚èé<div>b2</div>{/if}`) even as it breaks across lines, so it holds a different stable form for each authoring of one document.

Two corollaries specific to blocks, both following from "the boundary carries no signal":

- **Hug is all-or-nothing, across the whole construct.** A body welded to only the head, or only the tail, is not a half-expansion signal ‚Äî it converges like any other authoring ([if/hugged_boundary_convergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/hugged_boundary_convergence_prettier_divergence/)). And a branch that would render inline still drops to its own line once any *sibling* branch went multiline, so `{:else}` never welds its body while `{#if}` holds its own.
- **The body-expand decision is made by width alone, never by whether the head may wrap.** Those are orthogonal ‚Äî head-wrap is a property of the head, body layout a property of the body. Keying the body on the head's wrap-ability welded the body of any block following a *breakable* sibling ([expression_tag/adjacent_if_block_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/expression_tag/adjacent_if_block_long_prettier_divergence/) and its `{@html}` / `{@render}` siblings), where prettier's welded line only fits by breaking the body's inner call arguments. Welding is not merely the worse layout, it is **unstable**: the body then renders at the column where the over-width head ended, so its fill breaks at *every* separator, and re-formatting that output reads the newline it just injected as authored leading whitespace and settles on a different form ‚Äî an **F1 (idempotency) break**. Expanding is what makes the emitted form its own fixed point.

**And the rule reaches below layout: when the content fits, the boundary run is simply removed.** An inline element's authored boundary space is deleted, not preserved ‚Äî `<span> text </span>` ‚Üí `<span>text</span>`, uniformly with block elements and components ‚Äî because those authorings are the same document (the compiler trims every fragment edge at compile), and whenever tsv keeps content inline, every whitespace character in the output is one the compiler keeps. The run is trimmed whole (spaces, tabs, collapsing newlines), a whitespace-only element collapses (`<b> </b>` ‚Üí `<b></b>` ‚Äî and with wrapped attributes the close hugs, [inline_empty_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_empty_long_prettier_divergence/)), and the trim stops at content: an NBSP is content, a comment is a node (the space before a boundary comment is a fragment edge and trims; the space after it is inter-sibling and stays ‚Äî render-safe under `preserveComments` too), and a both-side newline-authored boundary around an element child keeps its layout meaning (want air ‚Üí author multiline). Prettier instead preserves an authored boundary space whenever the content fits ‚Äî the HTML/CSS inline whitespace model, which Svelte 5 deliberately broke from ‚Äî so the spaced authorings are prettier-stable forms tsv normalizes: [inline_boundary_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_boundary_whitespace_prettier_divergence/), including a `<title>` outside `<svelte:head>` ‚Äî a RegularElement, pinned separately because prettier's `<title>` handling could move independently: [title_boundary_whitespace](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/title_boundary_whitespace_prettier_divergence/) (the TitleElement form inside `<svelte:head>` prettier trims too, so only the regular form diverges) ‚Äî and the rest of prettier's whitespace-sensitive set (`<td>`, `<option>`, a foreign svg `<text>`): [inline_boundary_whitespace_misc](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_boundary_whitespace_misc_prettier_divergence/). Block elements, components, and `svelte:element` boundaries prettier trims too, so those agree. With this, no render-free boundary character survives anywhere in tsv's inline output, and `authoring_audit` asserts full authoring-independence at content boundaries (hug ‚Üî space ‚Üî newline reach one fixed point) everywhere outside `<pre>`/`<textarea>`.

**And it reaches inter-sibling whitespace in the one place that is *also* render-free: a whitespace-collapsing container.** Inside `<table>` / `<tbody>` / `<thead>` / `<tfoot>` / `<tr>` / `<colgroup>` / `<select>` / `<datalist>` (Svelte's `clean_nodes` `can_remove_entirely`) the compiler removes an inter-sibling whitespace-only run **entirely** rather than collapsing it to a rendered space, so it never renders. tsv lays such a container out **block-style** ‚Äî each child on its own indented line, the inter-sibling whitespace trimmed ‚Äî matching the compiled render, the same stance every other render-free boundary takes; prettier keeps a container authored inline on one line. An **authored blank line** between two children survives (collapsed to a single blank), because blank-line preservation is a Tier-2 authoring signal independent of render ‚Äî uniform with every other block-style boundary tsv produces. This is the **exact** Svelte set: a deliberate *subset* of what HTML collapses (Svelte's source carries a `// TODO others?`), so `optgroup` / `ul` / `ol` / `menu` / `dl` / `fieldset` are **not** members ‚Äî tsv keeps their inter-sibling space, matching Svelte (tsv is a drop-in for Svelte's compiler, not for raw HTML). The SVG arm of `can_remove_entirely` (any SVG element outside a `<text>` element) is namespace-based rather than name-based and is a follow-up; everywhere else an inter-sibling space is render-significant and stays. ‚Äî [ws_collapsing_containers](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/ws_collapsing_containers_prettier_divergence/) (`<select>` / `<table>` block-style, with an ordinary `<div>` control that keeps its space), [implicit_close_table](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/implicit_close_table_prettier_divergence/) (the same block-style over a table built with implicit end tags), the `<td>` / `<option>` cases of [inline_boundary_whitespace_misc](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_boundary_whitespace_misc_prettier_divergence/) (where the container block-style overlaps the boundary-space trim), and [ws_collapsing_container_blank](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/ws_collapsing_container_blank_prettier_divergence/) (an authored blank line between two `<option>`s is preserved block-style; prettier dangles the compact authoring).

Two consequences of "the boundary carries no signal":

- **A break on one side alone is not an expansion signal.** A component expands when the author broke **both** content boundaries; a lone opening newline collapses back inline rather than half-breaking the tags ([opening_newline_only](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/opening_newline_only_prettier_divergence/)). Prettier honors the lone break and dangles the closing delimiter to hold the content against it.
- **`svelte:*` elements are not special here.** `<slot>`, `<svelte:element>`, `<svelte:component>`, `<svelte:fragment>` and friends run the **same** layout analysis as regular elements, so they converge on the same block-style form. (They are block-kind for whitespace purposes: their content boundaries are trimmed, not preserved as a space. Prettier draws the same line from the other side ‚Äî its `isInlineElement` requires a `RegularElement`.)

**A CONTENT-boundary dangle survives in exactly one place: inside `<pre>` / `<textarea>`**, where that boundary whitespace *is* render-significant and the dangle is mandatory rather than cosmetic ‚Äî see [pre_closing_tag](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/pre_closing_tag/), [textarea_content_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/textarea_content_long/). Those elements never reach the shared layout analysis. An *empty* whitespace-sensitive element has no content to protect, so an inline parent hugging it lays out block-style like any other ([textarea_empty_hugged_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/textarea_empty_hugged_long_prettier_divergence/)).

**tsv does keep one dangle of its own, and it is not an exception to this rule** ‚Äî the **sibling `>` dangle** (`<a href={root}>Home</a‚èé>{#each ‚Ä¶}`), where an inline element byte-glued to a following sibling hands its closing `>` to that sibling's line: a multiline-rendering block head (as here), a following glued element (the G2 chain), or glued following text (the glued-both dangle in the break-before paragraph above). See [¬ßSvelte: Blocks](#svelte-blocks). The distinction is the whole point of this section: that dangle is keyed on **inter-sibling** whitespace ‚Äî specifically its *absence* ‚Äî and inter-sibling whitespace is render-**significant** under Svelte 5 (it collapses to one space; it does not vanish). So the character selecting that layout is one the compiler *keeps*, which is exactly the license a content-boundary character lacks. Same reason `authoring_audit` reshapes inter-sibling runs (space‚Üînewline) but *creates and destroys* content-boundary ones (hug‚Üîspace‚Üînewline).

Both formatters keep the block-style form once produced (`prettier(input) == input`); the divergence is that tsv *converges every authoring* to block-style while prettier dangles a compact authoring ‚Äî so these fixtures carry `unformatted_ours_*` compact variants (tsv normalizes them to the block-style input, prettier does not) alongside `prettier_variant_*` files pinning prettier's stable dangle form (which tsv likewise normalizes to the block-style input). See also the "Inline content (text)", "Inline content (expression)", and "Wide inline content + trailing text" rows above.

**The rule reaches the element's own *position*, not just its content: an opening tag never dangles after a space.** When an inline element is preceded by same-line inline content that must wrap, tsv breaks at the last **whitespace** boundary before the element ‚Äî carrying any *glued* prefix with it, whether a glued text word or a glued HTML **comment** (`<!--c--><a‚Ä¶>`, a run of them, or a word *and* a comment `word<!--c--><a‚Ä¶>` ‚Äî each binds to the element it precedes and moves to the fresh line as one unit) ‚Äî so the element starts a fresh line rather than leaving its opening tag stranded at the end of the text line. On its fresh line the element lays out uniformly with everything above: it collapses back inline when it fits, goes block-style when only its content overflows, and wraps its attributes when the opening tag itself exceeds printWidth. The whitespace boundary before the element is inter-node whitespace that collapses to one space at compile, so turning it into a break is render-equivalent (`ast_diff --render`); the *glued* boundary inside the run is render-significant and is never split (breaking there would inject a rendered space). Prettier keeps the opening tag on the text line ‚Äî hugging it and dropping only the content, or dangling its attributes/`>` ‚Äî and lets the line run past printWidth. tsv already preserves the fresh-line form when authored; the change is that it now *converges* the compact and dangled authorings to it. The one place an opening tag may still sit at a line end is after a **glued preceding element** whose own tag must wrap: there tsv dangles that preceding element's closing `>` onto the next element's line (`<span>foo</span‚èé><a‚Ä¶`, the **G2** shape), reusing the sibling-`>` dangle so nothing is stranded after a space. A run of 3+ glued elements is one indivisible unit: the whole run breaks before together (a wide element anywhere in it pulls the entire run to a fresh line ‚Äî no earlier short element can strand it on the text line), and every adjacent Soft pair sheds its `>` (a mid-run element both receives its predecessor's `>` and sheds its own). ‚Äî [inline_break_before_wrap_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_wrap_long_prettier_divergence/) (the HTML inline-element cases: control@100, collapse@101, last child, block-style, attrs-wrap), [inline_break_before_component_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_component_long_prettier_divergence/) (component parity), [inline_break_before_void_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_void_long_prettier_divergence/) (void / self-closing parity), [inline_break_before_glued_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_glued_long_prettier_divergence/) (a glued text prefix travels with the element ‚Äî never split), [inline_break_before_comment_glued_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_comment_glued_long_prettier_divergence/) (a glued HTML **comment** prefix travels with the element the same way ‚Äî `<!--c--><a‚Ä¶>` breaks before the comment, incl. a run of two comments and a block-style tail), [inline_break_before_comment_glued_word_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_comment_glued_word_long_prettier_divergence/) (a glued word *and* comment ‚Äî `word<!--c--><a‚Ä¶>` ‚Äî form one run that breaks before the word), [inline_break_before_gt_dangle_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_gt_dangle_long_prettier_divergence/) (the G2 closing-`>` dangle for a glued element pair), [inline_break_before_chain_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_chain_long_prettier_divergence/) (the G2 dangle generalized to a run of 3+ glued elements ‚Äî whole run breaks before, every pair sheds), [inline_closing_text](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_closing_text_prettier_divergence/) (a component with glued trailing text `.` collapses on its fresh line), [multiline_value_inline](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/multiline_value_inline_prettier_divergence/) + [_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/multiline_value_inline_long_prettier_divergence/) (the break is triggered by a forced-multiline *attribute* value, not width), [inline_nbsp_boundary_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_nbsp_boundary_long_prettier_divergence/) (the element collapses on its fresh line; a trailing NBSP stays glued to the close tag), [inline_break_before_nonterminal_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_break_before_nonterminal_long_prettier_divergence/) (a following whitespace-separated sibling ‚Äî the element still breaks before and block-styles; the terminal ` tail` hugs the intact close tag).

**The complement: an element *glued* to its predecessor breaks *after* itself.** With no whitespace boundary before it the break-before rule can't fire, so tsv breaks after the element instead ‚Äî the sibling-`>` dangle generalizes from a glued following *element* to glued following **text**. Glued on both sides (`text<span>x</span>text`), tsv dangles the closing `>` onto the following text's line (`<span>x</span‚èé>text`), the tag-internal analog of the trailing-space wrap ‚Äî the content stays inline and prettier produces the same form, so this is **not a divergence** ([inline_glued_both_dangle_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_glued_both_dangle_long/)). Two bounds return it to tsv's own layout, where prettier diverges: when the dangle line (`prefix<span>content</span`) would *itself* exceed printWidth (a wide prefix or wide content), dangling wouldn't help, so tsv lays out **block-style** where prettier double-dangles (`<span‚èé>x</span‚èé>`); and when the element is glued before but space-separated after, tsv **wraps at that trailing whitespace** where prettier keeps the over-width line ‚Äî [inline_glued_before_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_glued_before_long_prettier_divergence/) (the block-style side of the dangle boundary + the trailing-space wrap). Every boundary tsv moves is render-free (the content boundary is trimmed at compile, the trailing space collapses to one), so each AST is byte-identical.

- elements ‚Äî [inline_before_block_break_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_before_block_break_prettier_divergence/), [table_cell_hug_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/table_cell_hug_long_prettier_divergence/), [member_expr_break_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/member_expr_break_prettier_divergence/), [member_expr_break_order_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/member_expr_break_order_prettier_divergence/), [member_expr_break_order_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/member_expr_break_order_long_prettier_divergence/), [inline_with_if_block_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_with_if_block_prettier_divergence/), [inline_with_if_block_multiline_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_with_if_block_multiline_prettier_divergence/), [inline_if_content_block_style_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_if_content_block_style_prettier_divergence/), [inline_nested_else_if_block_style_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_nested_else_if_block_style_prettier_divergence/), [inline_nbsp_boundary_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_nbsp_boundary_long_prettier_divergence/), [inline_nested_child_trailing_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_nested_child_trailing_long_prettier_divergence/), [inline_content_unbreakable_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_content_unbreakable_prettier_divergence/), [inline_nested_wrap_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_nested_wrap_long_prettier_divergence/) (nested inline elements both wrap block-style; prettier double-pyramids), [inline_multiline_mixed_hug_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_multiline_mixed_hug_prettier_divergence/) (a hugged closing boundary still lays out block-style; prettier dangles), [inline_boundary_whitespace_multiline_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_boundary_whitespace_multiline_prettier_divergence/) (the boundary-whitespace authorings ‚Äî none / space / newline ‚Äî converge on one form), [inline_multiline_leading_text_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_multiline_leading_text_long_prettier_divergence/) (the same convergence when the content goes multiline by **width** rather than structurally ‚Äî a hugged element child at the closing boundary), [textarea_empty_hugged_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/textarea_empty_hugged_long_prettier_divergence/) (an *empty* `<textarea>` hugged by an inline `<label>`: nothing is whitespace-significant, so the label goes block-style; prettier's dangled `</label` suffix is what forces the textarea's attributes to wrap)
- components ‚Äî [compact_block_children_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/compact_block_children_prettier_divergence/), [compact_multiple_blocks_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/compact_multiple_blocks_prettier_divergence/), [inline_parent_blocks_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/inline_parent_blocks_prettier_divergence/), [text_child_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/text_child_long_prettier_divergence/) (component body long inline text wraps block-style; prettier dangles), [content_boundary_convergence_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/content_boundary_convergence_prettier_divergence/) (one document, three authorings: prettier keeps a stable form for each, tsv converges all three), [opening_newline_only_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/opening_newline_only_prettier_divergence/) (a break on one boundary only is not an expansion signal ‚Äî the content collapses back inline; prettier dangles the closing tag)
- special elements ‚Äî [attrs_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/attrs_long_prettier_divergence/) (`<svelte:component>` with a child, attributes wrapped), [svelte_element_hug_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/svelte_element_hug_long_prettier_divergence/) (`<svelte:element>` with long text content), [svelte_element_attrs_multiline_value_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/svelte_element_attrs_multiline_value_prettier_divergence/) (a multiline attribute value breaks the attributes; the content still goes block-style), [closing_tag_inline_content_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/closing_tag_inline_content_prettier_divergence/) (a `{#if}` sibling hugs the intact `</slot>` rather than a dangled `>`), [slot/expanding_no_ws_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special/slot/expanding_no_ws_prettier_divergence/) (a `<slot>` whose only child is an expanding block), [slot/block_children_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special/slot/block_children_prettier_divergence/) (a `<slot>` with block-element children goes multiline in parity with a `<span>` in the same shape ‚Äî the drift a private copy of the analysis had allowed)
- blocks ‚Äî [nested_expanding_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/nested_expanding_prettier_divergence/), [inline_element_boundary_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/inline_element_boundary_long_prettier_divergence/), [snippet/body_inline_content_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/snippet/body_inline_content_prettier_divergence/) (snippet body inline content lays out block-style; prettier dangles)
- block bodies (the second fragment family) ‚Äî [blocks/content_boundary_convergence_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/content_boundary_convergence_prettier_divergence/) (one document, four prettier forms, one tsv form ‚Äî across `{#if}` / `{#each}` / `{#key}` / `{#snippet}` / every `{#await}` phase and every `{:else if}` / `{:else}` branch), [blocks/if/hugged_boundary_convergence_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/hugged_boundary_convergence_prettier_divergence/) (the one-sided welds ‚Äî head-only, tail-only, and mixed-across-branches ‚Äî converge too: hug is all-or-nothing), [blocks/block_children_break_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/block_children_break_prettier_divergence/) (consecutive block-element children force the body to break; both formatters agree it breaks, only tsv keeps the tags intact), [expression_tag/adjacent_if_block_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/expression_tag/adjacent_if_block_long_prettier_divergence/) + [_html_tag_](../tests/fixtures/svelte/expression_tag/adjacent_if_block_html_tag_long_prettier_divergence/) + [_render_tag_](../tests/fixtures/svelte/expression_tag/adjacent_if_block_render_tag_long_prettier_divergence/) (a block after a breakable sibling: the body-expand decision is width's alone, so it lays out the same as with no sibling at all)
- attributes ‚Äî [multiline_value_inline_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/multiline_value_inline_prettier_divergence/), [directive_expr_logical_long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/directive_expr_logical_long_prettier_divergence/)
- directives ‚Äî [on/long_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/directives/on/long_prettier_divergence/)

### Svelte: Attributes

**Trailing comments in `{...}`** (‚óÜcontent_preservation) ‚Äî [expr_trailing](../tests/fixtures/svelte/syntax/comments/expr_trailing_prettier_divergence/) (block comments, inline); [expr_trailing_line](../tests/fixtures/svelte/syntax/comments/expr_trailing_line_prettier_divergence/) (line comments ‚Äî `}` kept on its own line so the `//` doesn't swallow it). Each fixture's README lists the contexts; they include `<svelte:element this={‚Ä¶}>` / `<svelte:component this={‚Ä¶}>`, whose expression Svelte's AST holds bare (no `ExpressionTag` around it) but which is the same `{‚Ä¶}` attribute value as any other. The *leading* and *interior* positions there are preserved by both formatters ‚Äî [expr_special_this](../tests/fixtures/svelte/syntax/comments/expr_special_this/).

**Leading/interior comments in a `bind:` function-binding sequence** (‚óÜcontent_preservation) ‚Äî `bind:value={getter, setter}` carries getter/setter expressions as a bare (parens-stripped) sequence; tsv preserves a comment at the author's position where prettier keeps it. A leading line or multi-line block comment, mid (between getter/setter) block, and mid line comment all match prettier (regular fixture [function_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/directives/bind/function_comment/)). A **single-line block** comment *leading* the sequence is the one divergence ‚Äî [function_comment_inline_block](../tests/fixtures/svelte/directives/bind/function_comment_inline_block_prettier_divergence/): prettier re-parenthesizes it (`{/* c */ (a, b)}`) then drops the comment on the next pass (non-idempotent), so tsv keeps the sequence bare and the comment in place. Trailing comments after the last operand are dropped by both. See [Comment Position Philosophy](#comment-position-philosophy).

**Multi-line block comment leading a parenthesized `{‚Ä¶}` value** (‚óÜcontent_preservation) ‚Äî a `{‚Ä¶}` expression value wrapped in redundant grouping parens whose *leading multi-line block comment* prettier drops as it strips the parens (`{a > b}`), across every `{‚Ä¶}` context: directive values (`bind:value={/* c‚èé*/ (a > b)}`, `class:active={‚Ä¶}`, and the other directive kinds) ‚Äî [value_paren_multiline_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/directives/value_paren_multiline_comment_prettier_divergence/) ‚Äî and expression tags (a plain `{expr}` template tag and the `style:` value Svelte models as one) ‚Äî [paren_multiline_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/expression_tag/paren_multiline_comment_prettier_divergence/). tsv strips the redundant parens too, but keeps the comment and reaches the same expanded fixed point the **bare** (no-paren) authoring produces ‚Äî there the comment is glued to its operand, both formatters already preserve it (a multi-line block forces the value to break), and that shared expanded form is each fixture's `input.svelte`, so the bare form is *not* a divergence. Only the paren-stripping path loses the comment: the parser leaves a discarded grouping `(`'s leading comment positional rather than owned, and the `{‚Ä¶}`-value gap emitters formerly emitted it inline without forcing the break ‚Äî the same class as the single-line function-binding case above, one level out. The one emitter that reindents+breaks a multi-line leading block, `build_leading_js_comment_doc`, is shared across **every** `{‚Ä¶}` context, so the same fix covers them all: the `{@html}` / `{@render}` tags ‚Äî [html_render_paren_multiline_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/tags/html_render_paren_multiline_comment_prettier_divergence/) ‚Äî the `{@attach}` / `{...spread}` attribute braces (one emitter, `build_braced_expression_doc`) ‚Äî [attach_spread_paren_multiline_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/attach_spread_paren_multiline_comment_prettier_divergence/) ‚Äî and the `{#if}` / `{#each}` / `{#key}` / `{#await}` block heads ‚Äî [head_paren_multiline_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/head_paren_multiline_comment_prettier_divergence/) (whose `input.svelte` also carries the pre-existing block-style layout of [¬ßSvelte: Blocks](#svelte-blocks), independent of the comment). **`{@const}` is the exception**: prettier *keeps* a `{@const}` value comment, so there is no comment loss ‚Äî only tsv's block-style enclosing-block layout diverges ‚Äî [const_paren_multiline_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/tags/const_paren_multiline_comment_prettier_divergence/); the fix there is purely the paren-form idempotency. ‚Äî See [Comment Position Philosophy](#comment-position-philosophy).

**Same-line `//` comment placement in the attribute list** (‚óÜcomment_preservation) ‚Äî [comment_same_line](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/comment_same_line_prettier_divergence/): a line comment the author put on the same line as the tag name (`<div // foo`) or trailing an attribute that has more attributes after it (`a="1" // mid`) stays trailing that token; prettier relocates it to its own line. A `//` trailing the *last* attribute (before `>`/`/>`) already stays inline in both formatters, so it is not a divergence ‚Äî [comment_trailing_same_line](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/comment_trailing_same_line/). Block comments and own-line comments are preserved as-written by both. See [Comment Position Philosophy](#comment-position-philosophy).

**Unofficial directive modifiers** (‚óÜcontent_preservation) ‚Äî a directive type *without* official modifier support ‚Äî `use:` / `bind:` / `class:` / `animate:` / `let:` ‚Äî carrying a `|modifier` (`use:action|mod`). Svelte's permissive parser records the trailing text in `modifiers`, and tsv's parser AST matches it exactly (so this is **not** a `_svelte_divergence`); but prettier-plugin-svelte silently *drops* the text on format, while tsv preserves it verbatim ‚Äî [modifier_preservation](../tests/fixtures/svelte/directives/modifier_preservation_prettier_divergence/). A `|modifier` is semantics-bearing source, not whitespace, so deleting it is content loss. The three officially-supporting types (`on:` / `transition:` / `style:`) keep their modifiers in both formatters; tsv emits and prints modifiers uniformly across all eight directive types. See [conformance_svelte.md ¬ßDirective Modifiers](./conformance_svelte.md#directive-modifiers).

**Attribute value containing a literal `"`** (‚óÜprettier_bug / content_corruption) ‚Äî a quoted attribute or `style:` value whose (single-quote-authored) raw text contains a literal `"` ‚Äî `attr='a"b'`, `class='c"d'`, `style:content='"x"'`. tsv defaults attribute delimiters to double quotes (`'value'` ‚Üí `"value"`, matching prettier-plugin-svelte) but switches to **single** quotes for the one value shape double quotes cannot hold ‚Äî HTML ¬ß13.1.2.3 requires a double-quoted value to contain no literal `"`, and single-quoted attribute values are an equal first-class syntax. prettier-plugin-svelte instead re-wraps the value in `"` unconditionally, so the interior `"` closes the value early and the output is corrupted markup that **does not re-parse** (`prettier(output)` throws) ‚Äî a semantic change, and prettier's own `html` / `vue` / `angular` formatters keep single quotes here, so only the svelte plugin regresses it. The rule is total and lossless: in valid source a value's raw text carries at most one literal quote kind (the delimiter quote must appear as an entity inside ‚Äî `&apos;`/`&quot;` ‚Äî which tsv preserves verbatim), so a `"`-bearing value never also has a literal `'` and no escaping is ever needed; single quotes surface *only* for values that literally cannot be double-quoted. Plain attributes / `class` / component props / multi-part values ‚Äî [attributes/value_double_quote](../tests/fixtures/svelte/attributes/value_double_quote_prettier_divergence/); `style:` directive values ‚Äî [directives/style/value_double_quote](../tests/fixtures/svelte/directives/style/value_double_quote_prettier_divergence/); `<svelte:element>` plain-string `this=` values ‚Äî [special_elements/svelte_element_this_double_quote](../tests/fixtures/svelte/special_elements/svelte_element_this_double_quote_prettier_divergence/).

### Svelte: Blocks

Standalone head wrap + dangle + body-expand:

- `{#each}` ‚Äî [each_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/each/long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#await}` ‚Äî [await_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#key}` ‚Äî [key_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/key/long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#if}` (binary / member chain / call / `{:else if}`) ‚Äî [if_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#if}` last block quirk ‚Äî [last_block](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/last_block_prettier_divergence/)

The shape is keyed on **that the head broke, not on why**: tsv's block head hugs its first
fragment to `{#if`, indents what follows, and drops `}` to base ‚Äî whether the break came from
printWidth or from a comment. A head far under printWidth still takes that shape when a *line*
comment forces the break. (A **multi-line block** comment's newlines live inside its verbatim
source span, which renders with no context indent by design, so its continuation is the
comment's own line and only the `}` dangle shows; a **single-line block** comment breaks
nothing and the head stays inline, both formatters agreeing.) Prettier never dangles a block
head's `}` whatever broke it, so this is the one divergence on a second trigger ‚Äî not a
print-width tolerance:

- `{#if}` (comment-forced head break) ‚Äî [if/condition_breaking_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/condition_breaking_comment_prettier_divergence/)

Same layout inside an inline element (head wraps + body expands, element hugs the outer boundary):

- `{#if}` ‚Äî [if/inline_element_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/inline_element_long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#each}` ‚Äî [each/inline_element_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/each/inline_element_long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#key}` ‚Äî [key/inline_element_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/key/inline_element_long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#await}` ‚Äî [await/inline_element_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/inline_element_long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#snippet}` (params inline + body expand vs prettier's param-wrap) ‚Äî [snippet/inline_element_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/snippet/inline_element_long_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#snippet}` standalone, **flush body** (tsv keeps params inline + body on its own line; prettier wraps the params just to keep the body hugging `)}`) ‚Äî [snippet/flush_body_param_wrap_prettier_divergence](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/snippet/flush_body_param_wrap_prettier_divergence/)

**‚óÜprint_width.** Prettier doesn't apply width-based wrapping to block expressions at all:

- **Method chains** in `{#each}`, `{#await}`, `{#if}`, `{#key}`, etc. don't account for the tag prefix width, resulting in 140+ char lines. tsv passes context offset for proper wrapping.
- **Logical expressions** (`&&`, `||`) in block conditions are never wrapped internally by Prettier, even when exceeding 100 chars. (In `<script>`, assignments provide a break point so this isn't an issue.) tsv wraps them with proper indentation.
- **Function calls** in block expressions don't wrap their arguments. tsv wraps function arguments when they exceed print width.

**Head `}` dangle + clause hug.** When a block head wraps, tsv drops the closing `}` (and any `as item` / `then value` clause) to its own line at the tag's base indent ‚Äî `{#if a &&‚èé\t‚Ä¶‚èé}`, `{#each ‚Ä¶‚èéas item}` ‚Äî consistent with tsv's JS `if (‚èé‚Ä¶‚èé) {` and its broken-element `>` (`bracketSameLine: false`). The one shape that hugs is a single call/`new` whose arguments wrapped: its `)` already dedents to base, so the clause + `}` continue on it (`) as item}`, `)}`, `) then r}`). Prettier never wraps a block head, so it never faces this.

**Body-expand (whole construct goes multiline).** When the head wraps ‚Äî or the inline construct simply exceeds printWidth, or the body breaks for any other reason ‚Äî tsv expands the **entire** block: the body, every `{:then}` / `{:catch}` / `{:else}` / `{:else if}` section/branch, and the `{/tag}` close each drop to their own indented lines, uniformly across `{#if}` / `{#each}` / `{#await}` / `{#key}` / `{#snippet}`. The decision is **all-or-nothing and width-driven**: the body boundary is render-free (see [¬ßSvelte: Inline content block-style](#svelte-inline-content-block-style)), so neither the whitespace the author wrote there nor the head's wrap-ability may select it ‚Äî a block following a breakable sibling expands exactly as it would standalone. This holds **inside inline elements/components too** (`<span>{#if ‚Ä¶}‚Ä¶{/if}</span>`) ‚Äî block-body boundary whitespace is render-non-significant there (verified against the Svelte compiler), so it is safe; the only gate is `<pre>` / `white-space:pre`, where the drop is suppressed and the body stays on the line (both formatters agree ‚Äî [elements/pre_block_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/pre_block_body_long/)). Inside `<pre>` a nested element's wrapped attributes and close token indent off its nesting depth ‚Äî one level per enclosing container, the same model as prettier ([elements/pre_nested_attr_indent](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/pre_nested_attr_indent/)) ‚Äî and the source close form is preserved (self-closing `/>` vs explicit `></tag>`), for components and HTML inline elements alike. One residual divergence remains there: an empty self-closing element whose attributes fit within printWidth (counting the preserved-text prefix on the line) keeps them on one line with only `/>` dropping, where prettier full-breaks them regardless ‚Äî [elements/pre_block_empty_element](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/pre_block_empty_element_prettier_divergence/). Prettier keeps the construct inline past printWidth (only the enclosing element wraps).

**Middle zone (head fits alone, head + body doesn't).** tsv decouples the head-wrap decision (head-alone width) from the body-expand decision (head + body width): when the head fits on its own line but the whole construct overflows, the head stays flat and only the body expands. This is chosen in one pass (no wrap-then-unwrap across two formats), so every layout is an idempotent fixed point.

**Uniform body drop (no breakable-element hug).** When an inline-authored block body overflows, tsv drops it to its own indented line **uniformly ‚Äî for every body shape**: text, expression tags (`{x}`), void/empty elements (`<Spinner />`, `<Comp></Comp>`), and elements/components **with attributes or children** alike. Prettier instead leaves the body hugging the `}` and breaks it *internally* (an element wraps its attributes / closing `>`; text just overflows) ‚Äî prettier's block-body layout is driven by authored boundary whitespace, never by width. tsv's uniform drop keeps the layout idempotent (a one-pass `conditional_group`, no special case keyed on whether the body can break internally) and consistent across all body shapes and contexts (block level, inside inline elements/components, in any section/branch). tsv does not hug a breakable body element: as a non-first body node (behind leading text, a comment, a void sibling, or an atomic `{:else}` branch) hugging over-wraps the head and is non-idempotent across two passes. Cataloged at [if/element_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/element_body_long_prettier_divergence/) and [each/element_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/each/element_body_long_prettier_divergence/) (block level, at the 100/101 boundary), [await/element_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/element_body_long_prettier_divergence/) and [snippet/element_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/snippet/element_body_long_prettier_divergence/) (inside `<Container>`), [await/full_form_element_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/full_form_element_body_long_prettier_divergence/) (the full `{:then}`/`{:catch}` form, each section body drops), [key/void_element_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/key/void_element_body_long_prettier_divergence/) (void body + an attributed body that drops the same way), [elements/inline_if_sibling_fill_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_if_sibling_fill_long_prettier_divergence/) (body drop next to an inline sibling), [elements/inline_component_else_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_component_else_body_long_prettier_divergence/) (breakable element in `{:else}`, behind an atomic consequent), [if/element_body_leading_node_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/element_body_leading_node_long_prettier_divergence/) (non-first body node ‚Äî leading text, a comment, or a void element before the breakable element), and [if/element_body_deep_nested](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/element_body_deep_nested_prettier_divergence/) (deep nesting ‚Äî the dropped element re-wraps at the body indent). Paramless `{#snippet}` bodies drop the same way once the whole construct still overflows after the element boundary wraps ‚Äî [snippet/inline_element_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/snippet/inline_element_long_prettier_divergence/). The drop reads correctly embedded in realistic nested context with inline siblings (incl. the breadcrumb shape) ‚Äî [elements/block_body_drop_nested_siblings](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/block_body_drop_nested_siblings_prettier_divergence/).

**Sibling `>` dangle (axis 3).** When an inline element is immediately followed ‚Äî no whitespace ‚Äî by a block that **renders multiline**, tsv dangles that element's **closing `>`** onto the block-head line (`<a href={root}>Home</a‚èé>{#each ‚Ä¶}`). This applies to **all five block heads** ‚Äî `{#if}` / `{#each}` / `{#key}` / `{#await}` / `{#snippet}`. It generalizes the rule tsv already applies from the enclosing-element side: the `>` token immediately preceding a block's `{#‚Ä¶}` dangles, whether it's the *opening* `>` of a parent inline element holding a sole-content block (`<span‚èé>{#if ‚Ä¶}`) or the *closing* `>` of a preceding inline sibling. The `>` moves only *inside* the closing tag (`</a‚èé>`), so the boundary whitespace is tag-internal and the output parses to a byte-identical AST ‚Äî render-safe (verified against the Svelte compiler), the same property as the element boundary-`>` wrap. It is **strict / multiline-only**: a short block that stays inline keeps the `>` hugged (`<span>text</span>{#if c}text{/if}`), and the decision keys on whether the block actually renders multiline ‚Äî not on whether its body is authored inline or on its own line ‚Äî so the layout is a fixed point on its own output. It is **leading-side only**: the closing side (`{/if}<span>`) keeps flowing. Text/expression siblings (`wide text {#if‚Ä¶}`, `{x}{#if‚Ä¶}`) keep hugging ‚Äî there is no `>` to dangle and the boundary whitespace is render-fixed, an asymmetry that is forced, not a tsv inconsistency. Prettier never expands the block at all, so it always keeps the boundary hugged. **`{#await}` / `{#snippet}` parity:** unlike `{#if}` / `{#each}` / `{#key}`, await/snippet don't force their block parent multiline on their own (a lone `<div>{#await p}x{/await}</div>` stays inline, matching prettier) ‚Äî they go multiline only once they follow a **breakable** sibling: an inline element / component / expression-or-`{@html}`-or-`{@render}` tag (the `has_preceding_breakable` set). There the parent breaks so the dangle, the block-on-own-line separation for a block sibling, and the body-drop all resolve in one pass. `has_preceding_breakable` reaches only the **head** (it holds the head flat, so the sibling breaks first); the **body**-drop is width's decision alone and never keys on it ‚Äî see [¬ßBody-expand](#svelte-blocks) above. After a **non-breakable** sibling ‚Äî plain text or a comment ‚Äî they stay **inline**, matching prettier; the force is additionally gated on `kind.is_block()`, so an inline element or component parent never breaks for *any* sibling. This is a distinct axis from the `>` dangle above: a breakable sibling breaks the *parent* even when the short block keeps its own `>` hugged, and that break is itself a divergence (prettier keeps the short inline-authored construct inline). Cataloged at [elements/inline_sibling_gt_dangle](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_sibling_gt_dangle_prettier_divergence/) (the dangle for all five heads + a no-dangle control), [elements/await_snippet_breakable_sibling](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/await_snippet_breakable_sibling_prettier_divergence/) (the short-case parent break after a breakable sibling), [elements/await_snippet_nonbreakable_sibling_inline](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/await_snippet_nonbreakable_sibling_inline/) (the non-breakable text/comment counterpart that stays inline, matching prettier), [components/await_snippet_sibling_inline](../tests/fixtures/svelte/components/await_snippet_sibling_inline/) (a component parent stays inline for any sibling, incl. `{@const}` / `{@debug}`), [blocks/await/preceding_sibling_body_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/preceding_sibling_body_long_prettier_divergence/) (await body-drop after a non-danglable expression-tag sibling), [elements/block_body_drop_nested_siblings](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/block_body_drop_nested_siblings_prettier_divergence/) (the breadcrumb `</a>` dangle in realistic context), and [elements/inline_if_sibling_fill_long](../tests/fixtures/svelte/elements/inline_if_sibling_fill_long_prettier_divergence/) (the `</span>` dangle in a fill). The **inline counterpart** of the dangle ‚Äî a preceding sibling before an inline-rendering `{#await}` ‚Äî **hugs** the `>` (`</a>{#await ‚Ä¶}`) rather than dangling it. The `>` must always be **placed, never dropped** ‚Äî a dropped `>` (`</a{#await ‚Ä¶}`) is unreparseable. `{#await}` reaches this on two paths, both handled: the empty-await path (a short empty block hugs; a long head that width-wraps dangles ‚Äî a *render-time* decision `will_break` can't see, so it's an `if_break`-in-`group`) and the space-only path (a `group` that hugs when it fits). Cataloged at [blocks/await/empty_sibling_gt](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/empty_sibling_gt/) (a bare empty `{#await promise}{/await}` after a sibling ‚Äî the `>` hugged in parity with prettier; its space-only-authoring variants exercise the space-only path).

**Empty `{#await}` sections (‚óÜcorrectness on `:catch`).** An **empty-body `:then`** ‚Äî `{#await p} {:then v}{/await}`, or the shorthand `{#await p then v}{/await}` ‚Äî is **dropped**, marker and binding, collapsing to `{#await p}{/await}` in parity with prettier (the `value` binding is unused when nothing renders; a *space-only* pending folds to the same fixed point via `await_shorthand`, while a *newline*-authored one keeps its full multiline form). But an **empty `:catch` is kept** (`{#await p}‚Ä¶{:catch e}{/await}`) ‚Äî a deliberate divergence from prettier, which deletes it too. An empty `{:catch}` still **handles** a rejection (renders nothing); deleting it lets the rejection **propagate** instead ‚Äî a semantic change, so tsv preserves the section (correctness over conformance). Kept the same way whether the construct is inline or **block-style**: the section's boundary separators are soft, so inline the empty section collapses and its markers glue (`{#await p}x{:catch e}{/await}`), while in block form it keeps its own line like any other section ‚Äî `{:catch e}` and `{/await}` each on a line, the empty body's blank line between. Cataloged at [blocks/await/empty_catch](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/empty_catch_prettier_divergence/) (inline) and [blocks/await/empty_catch_multiline](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/empty_catch_multiline_prettier_divergence/) (block form).

**Empty branch, block form (‚óÜdesign_choice).** An empty branch of `{#if}` / `{:else if}` / `{:else}`, and an empty `{#each}` body or `{:else}` fallback, keeps its own line inside a **block-form** construct: the marker and the close each sit on a line, with the empty body's blank line between (`{:else}‚èé‚èé{/if}`). tsv normalizes to that shape **whatever the author wrote at the branch boundary**, so a glued and a newline-authored empty branch reach one fixed point. Prettier instead **preserves** the authored boundary ‚Äî it leaves a newline-authored branch in exactly that shape (tsv agrees) but keeps a **glued** one glued. tsv declines that preservation because an empty branch renders nothing, so the whitespace inside it is **render-free** and must not select the layout ‚Äî the same principle as the all-or-nothing body-expand above. **Inline** the separators vanish and the branch collapses instead ([blocks/if/empty](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/empty/) pins `{#if a}<div>text</div>{:else}{/if}`, which both formatters produce) ‚Äî one soft-separator rule, two renderings. A branch carrying content is untouched. Cataloged at [blocks/empty_branch_collapse](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/empty_branch_collapse_prettier_divergence/).

**Space-only section boundaries glue inline (‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî Svelte-mirror trim).** A space-only content boundary in a block section is **render-free** ‚Äî the compiler trims every fragment edge at compile (`clean_nodes`) ‚Äî so tsv removes it in inline layout: `{#if a} x {/if}` ‚Üí `{#if a}x{/if}`, uniformly across `{#if}` / `{:else if}` / `{:else}` / `{#each}` (+ fallback) / `{#key}` / every `{#await}` phase / `{#snippet}`. A render-free character neither survives in the output nor selects the layout; a **newline**-authored boundary keeps its meaning (the construct stays multiline) ‚Äî a space is not intent. Prettier's own treatment splits by family: it **expands** a symmetric-spaced `{#if}` / `{#each}` / `{#key}` / `{#snippet}` body to multiline ‚Äî a render-free space selecting the whole construct's form ‚Äî with a quirk (the last block in a file stays inline as authored), yet it **preserves** a spaced `{#await}` inline, keeping a space the compiler deletes. (The split is a plugin artifact, not a stance: every block fragment maps a spaced boundary to the same `line` doc, but the plugin's `AwaitBlock` printer is the one block case built without the `breakParent` the `IfBlock`/`EachBlock`/`KeyBlock` cases carry, so only await's `line`s can collapse.) tsv glues consistently regardless of family or position. Same render-free principle as the empty-branch normalization above, and the same trim an inline element's content boundary gets (see [¬ßSvelte: Inline content block-style](#svelte-inline-content-block-style)). Cataloged at [blocks/boundary_space_trim](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/boundary_space_trim_prettier_divergence/) (the expanding if-family) and [blocks/await/boundary_space_trim](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/boundary_space_trim_prettier_divergence/) (the preserving await, incl. the `then` shorthand); [blocks/if/spaces](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/if/spaces_prettier_divergence/) is the if-family maximal injection ‚Äî a space at every collapsible position at once (tag-internal + block-element content boundary + section boundary), across div/text/`{:else if}`/space-only-empty shapes.

### Svelte: destructuring literal normalization

**‚óÜdesign_choice.** tsv routes the binding patterns of `{#each ‚Ä¶ as}`, `{#await ‚Ä¶ then}`, `{:then}`, and `{:catch}` through its TypeScript printer, so **literal default values** normalize to tsv's canonical form ‚Äî string literals to single quotes (`{ a = "x" }` ‚Üí `{ a = 'x' }`, with escape-minimizing keeping double quotes when single would need escaping, so `"a'b"` stays double) and numeric literals to canonical shape (lowercase hex/exponent, leading/trailing-zero rules: `0xFF` ‚Üí `0xff`, `1.50` ‚Üí `1.5`, `.5` ‚Üí `0.5`, `1E10` ‚Üí `1e10`, `0xFFn` ‚Üí `0xffn`). This is the same normalization `{@const}` (and every other literal tsv emits) already applies. prettier-plugin-svelte instead prints these patterns from raw source, preserving the author's quote style and numeric token verbatim ‚Äî in these binding positions it ignores `singleQuote` and numeric normalization. tsv normalizes uniformly so a destructuring default reads the same wherever it appears. Booleans, `null`, and regex literals are already canonical in both formatters and are unaffected.

- `{#each as { x = ‚Ä¶ }}` strings + numbers ‚Äî [destructure_literal_default](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/each/destructure_literal_default_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#await then}` / `{:then}` / `{:catch}` strings + numbers ‚Äî [destructure_literal_default](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/destructure_literal_default_prettier_divergence/)

### Svelte: destructuring rename-with-default key drop

**‚óÜprettier_bug.** A renamed (non-shorthand) destructuring property that carries a **default value** loses its source key in prettier-plugin-svelte's binding-pattern printer for `{#each ‚Ä¶ as}`, `{#await ‚Ä¶ then}`, `{:then}`, and `{:catch}`. `{ a: b = 1 }` (read property `a`, bind to `b`) prints as `{ b = 1 }` (read property `b`) ‚Äî a **semantic change**, since the output reads a different source property. The bug is specific to a non-shorthand property whose value is an `AssignmentPattern`: plain renames without a default (`{ a: b }`) print correctly, only the defaulted property in a list loses its key (`{ a: b = 1, c: d }` ‚Üí `{ b = 1, c: d }`), and a nested pattern with a default drops its key the same way (`{ a: { b } = c }` ‚Üí `{ { b } = c }`). prettier's wrong output is itself stable. tsv prints these patterns through its TypeScript printer, which preserves the key in every case.

- `{#each as}` rename + default, sibling, nested ‚Äî [destructure_rename_default](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/each/destructure_rename_default_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#await then}` / `{:then}` / `{:catch}` rename + default ‚Äî [destructure_rename_default](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/destructure_rename_default_prettier_divergence/)

### Svelte: destructuring binding-pattern comments

**‚óÜcontent_preservation.** A comment placed **inside** a destructuring binding pattern of `{#each ‚Ä¶ as}`, `{#await ‚Ä¶ then}`, `{:then}`, or `{:catch}` is preserved where the author wrote it; prettier-plugin-svelte prints these patterns from a comment-blind path and silently drops it. tsv routes the pattern through a comment-aware printer (the same canonical positions it preserves for a regular TypeScript destructure, e.g. `const { a = /* c */ 1 } = x`), so a destructuring comment reads the same wherever it appears. Covered (block comments, pattern stays inline): object default value (`{ a = /* c */ 1 }`), leading after `{` (`{ /* c */ a }`), trailing before `}` (`{ a /* c */ }`), rename `key:`‚Üívalue gap (`{ a: /* c */ b }`), array element (`[a /* c */]`), rest binding (`[.../* c */ rest]`), and nested patterns. Per [Comment Position Philosophy](#comment-position-philosophy), user intent is preserved when prettier moves or drops comments. (In the `{#await ‚Ä¶ then}` *shorthand* pattern, the awaited expression's trailing-comment range stops at the pattern, so an interior comment is not pulled out to trail the expression.) These are `_svelte_prettier_divergence` fixtures: acorn attaches the comment to the pattern node (`leadingComments`/`trailingComments`) where tsv's detached model does not ‚Äî see [conformance_svelte.md ¬ßComment Attachment Differences](./conformance_svelte.md#comment-attachment-differences).

- `{#each as { ‚Ä¶ }}` object/array/rest/nested positions ‚Äî [destructure_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/each/destructure_comment_svelte_prettier_divergence/)
- `{#await then}` / `{:then}` / `{:catch}` ‚Äî [destructure_comment](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/await/destructure_comment_svelte_prettier_divergence/)

### Svelte: empty destructuring brace spacing

**‚óÜdesign_choice.** Non-empty object-destructure patterns in `{#each ‚Ä¶ as}`, `{#await ‚Ä¶ then}`, `{:then}`, and `{:catch}` binding positions space their braces in both formatters (`{a}` ‚Üí `{ a }`), matching prettier-plugin-svelte under `bracketSpacing`. The lone remaining divergence is the **empty** pattern: tsv keeps tight braces (`{}`), prettier-plugin-svelte inserts a space (`{ }`). tsv's empty object braces stay tight everywhere ‚Äî `bracketSpacing` only spaces braces around content, and an empty pattern has none ‚Äî so this binding position follows the same universal empty-braces rule as an empty object literal (`{}`) and a TypeScript empty destructure (`const {} = x`, where both formatters already agree on `{}`).

- `{#each as {}}` empty pattern ‚Äî [destructure_empty](../tests/fixtures/svelte/blocks/each/destructure_empty_prettier_divergence/)

### TypeScript

- Empty statement blank lines ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [empty_standalone](../tests/fixtures/typescript/statements/empty_standalone_prettier_divergence/)
- Return type generic union ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [return_type_generic_union_long](../tests/fixtures/typescript/declarations/function/return_type_generic_union_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Single specifier import ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [single_specifier_long](../tests/fixtures/typescript/modules/imports/single_specifier_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Module path calls ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [path_calls_long](../tests/fixtures/typescript/modules/imports/path_calls_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Trailing member after object-arg call ‚Äî ‚óÜprint_width ‚Äî [trailing_member_expand_args_long](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/calls/chained/trailing_member_expand_args_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Instantiation expression parens ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [instantiation_parens](../tests/fixtures/typescript/typescript_specific/assertions/instantiation_parens_prettier_divergence/), [export_default_instantiation](../tests/fixtures/typescript/modules/exports/default_wrappable_leftmost_operators/instantiation_prettier_divergence/)
- Non-null parenthesized base ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [non_null_paren_base_long](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/member/non_null_paren_base_long_prettier_divergence/)
- Constrained infer extends-operand parens ‚Äî ‚óÜprettier_bug ‚Äî [constrained_extends_parens](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/infer/constrained_extends_parens_prettier_divergence/)
- Arrow type param trailing comma ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [single_type_param](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/arrow/generic/single_type_param_prettier_divergence/)
- Empty-object comment bracket spacing ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [empty_block_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/objects/empty_block_comment_prettier_divergence/), [destructure empty_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/destructuring/empty_comment_prettier_divergence/), [enum empty_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/declarations/enum/body_empty_comment_prettier_divergence/), [literal_body_empty](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/comments/literal_body_empty_prettier_divergence/), [union_empty_object_member](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/union_empty_object_member_prettier_divergence/), [call_type_arg_empty_comment](../tests/fixtures/typescript/typescript_specific/generics/call_type_arg_empty_comment_prettier_divergence/)
- Optional rest parameter `?` ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [rest_optional_param](../tests/fixtures/typescript/typescript_specific/rest_optional_param_prettier_divergence/)
- ES2015+ identifier property keys ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚óÜspec_precedence ‚Äî [property_key_es2015_ident](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/objects/property_key_es2015_ident_prettier_divergence/)
- Non-null optional-chain bare strip ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [optional_paren_non_null_bare](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/chain/optional_paren_non_null_bare_prettier_divergence/)
- Class field key unquoting ‚Äî ‚óÜdesign_choice ‚Äî [field_key_unquote](../tests/fixtures/typescript/declarations/class/field_key_unquote_prettier_divergence/)

**Instantiation expression parens**: Prettier strips parentheses from ternary and binary expressions in `TSInstantiationExpression` (`(x ? y : z)<T>` ‚Üí `x ? y : z<T>`), changing semantics. Without parens, `<T>` only applies to the last operand. tsv preserves parens to maintain the original meaning. Both formatters agree on preserving parens for assignment expressions (`(x = y)<T>`). A class-expression operand in `export default` position ‚Äî `export default (class {}<T>)` ‚Äî is the same bug but sharper: stripping the parens makes the leading `class {}` a class _declaration_, so Prettier's output re-parses to a `ClassDeclaration` plus a dangling `<T>;` statement (a different AST), while tsv keeps the parens (adjudicated by `export_default_needs_parens`; see [export_default_instantiation](../tests/fixtures/typescript/modules/exports/default_wrappable_leftmost_operators/instantiation_prettier_divergence/)).

**Constrained infer extends-operand parens**: An `infer X extends C` only ever appears in a conditional type's extends-type, so a trailing token always follows the constraint. When a _nested_ arrow's return abuts the enclosing `? :`, the parens TypeScript requires are the only thing keeping the parse unambiguous, and Prettier strips them, emitting output that **fails to re-parse** (acorn-typescript rejects it): `M extends (() => () => infer U extends string) ? ‚Ä¶` ‚Üí `M extends () => () => infer U extends string ? ‚Ä¶` (Prettier's `needs-parentheses` rule only inspects the immediate return type). tsv keeps the parens, staying valid. Two related forms are preserved by both formatters: the _conditional-type_ infer constraint (`X extends infer U extends (A extends B ? C : D) ? ‚Ä¶` ‚Äî Prettier keeps these parens) and the single-arrow return (`M extends (() => infer U extends string) ? ‚Ä¶` ‚Äî Prettier's single-level rule covers it; see [constrained_extends_parens](../tests/fixtures/typescript/types/infer/constrained_extends_parens/), where tsv matches). A bare `<T extends (A extends B ? C : D)>` type-parameter declaration is unaffected: the `>` terminates it, so Prettier strips and tsv matches.

**Single specifier import**: Prettier intentionally keeps single-specifier imports on one line even when they exceed print width ([prettier/prettier#1954](https://github.com/prettier/prettier/issues/1954#issuecomment-306067705)). tsv wraps at print width for consistency and to respect the configured line length limit.

**Module path calls**: Prettier special-cases `require`/`import` identifiers:

- `require(string)`: Prettier keeps on one line regardless of length; tsv wraps at print width
- `require.resolve.paths(string)`: Prettier breaks at `.paths` chain; tsv expands call arguments
- `import.meta.resolve(string)`: Prettier breaks at `.resolve` chain; tsv expands call arguments

tsv treats these like any other function call‚Äîno special-casing for module path identifiers. This is consistent with tsv's handling of single-specifier imports: respect print width uniformly.

**Trailing member after a call with an object argument**: When `X.f({‚Ä¶}).member` exceeds print width ‚Äî the call's arguments fit inline, but appending the trailing member overflows ‚Äî Prettier keeps the arguments on one line and breaks the member onto its own indented line (`.member`), while tsv expands the object argument and keeps the member on the closing brace (`}).member`). This is the same stance as Module path calls above (and single-specifier imports): tsv wraps a call's arguments the same way regardless of a trailing member, rather than special-casing the chain. Because Prettier preserves a multiline object, it keeps tsv's expanded form stable too, so the two only diverge from compact or Prettier-authored source ‚Äî the Prettier form is pinned as a `prettier_variant` (Prettier keeps it stable; tsv normalizes it back to `input`). Fixture: [trailing_member_expand_args_long](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/calls/chained/trailing_member_expand_args_long_prettier_divergence/).

**Non-null parenthesized base**: For a non-null assertion on a parenthesized base whose inner call breaks its arguments (`(await call(...))!.member`), Prettier hugs the inner call (`(await call(\n...\n))!.member`) ‚Äî yet it _hangs_ the outer parens for the same base without the `!` (`(await call(...)).member`, see [paren_base_trailing_long](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/member/paren_base_trailing_long/), where tsv matches Prettier). tsv lays out the parenthesized base the same way regardless of a trailing non-null assertion, keeping the two forms visually consistent. Content is identical (ASTs match); only the parenthesized-base layout differs.

**Non-null assertion in optional-chain parens**: A non-null `!` on a **bare** parenthesized optional chain ‚Äî one with no trailing non-optional access ‚Äî has redundant parens: the `!` is TypeScript-only and applies to the whole chain regardless (`(a?.b)!` ‚â° `a?.b!`), so tsv strips them (`(a?.b)!` ‚Üí `a?.b!`, and the `!`-inside form `(a?.b!)` ‚Üí `a?.b!`). Prettier keeps the parens on `(a?.b)!` (it strips only `(a?.b!)`). tsv matches Biome. When a **non-optional access follows** (`(a?.b)!.c`), the parens are required ‚Äî they seal the chain so `.c` isn't short-circuited (`(a?.b)!.c` vs `a?.b!.c`) ‚Äî and there both formatters keep the parens and preserve the author's `!` placement (inside or outside: `(a?.b!).c` and `(a?.b)!.c` each stay as written), so that case is not a divergence. Content is identical (ASTs match); only the redundant parens differ. Fixtures: [optional_paren_non_null_bare](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/chain/optional_paren_non_null_bare_prettier_divergence/) (the strip), [optional_paren_non_null_boundary](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/chain/optional_paren_non_null_boundary/) and [optional_paren_non_null_inside](../tests/fixtures/typescript/expressions/chain/optional_paren_non_null_inside/) (required parens, both preserved).

**Return type generic union**: Prettier has special handling for `null` and `void` in union types within generic return types. When the second union member is `null` or `void`: (1) function declarations and class methods allow lines to exceed print width instead of breaking inside `<>`, (2) arrow functions break the assignment (`const fn =`) instead of breaking inside the return type. tsv breaks consistently inside the return type generic at the print width boundary regardless of type keyword.

**Arrow type param trailing comma**: For a generic arrow with a **single type param that has no constraint** (`<T>`, default-only `<T = string>`, or `const`-modified `<const T>`), Prettier forces a trailing comma ‚Äî `<T,>` ‚Äî via `shouldForceTrailingComma` (`language-js/print/type-parameters.js`).
